# Current Capabilities

This page is the human-readable summary of the current GameEngine capability contract. The machine-readable source of truth is `engine/agent/manifest.json`; use `pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File tools/agent-context.ps1` when an agent needs exact fields, recipe ids, command surfaces, host gates, or validation commands.

Environment commercial aggregate status: Environment Highest Commercial Readiness v1 Tasks 1-32 now close the exact clean-break commercial environment matrix through reviewed package/host evidence. The selected rows for strict Vulkan aggregate readiness, Apple-host Metal aggregate readiness, clean-break Metal aggregate readiness, backend parity v2, Windows D3D12, Windows Vulkan, Linux Vulkan, macOS Metal, iOS Metal, Android Vulkan, exact platform readiness, exact all-platform readiness, broad measured optimization, AAA preset asset library, full OpenEXR/KTX2/Basis asset pipeline, physical weather simulation, and production artist workflow are ready. Task 32 closes Android Vulkan through `tools/validate-android-vulkan-runtime-host.ps1 -RequireReady` on an Android Emulator primary `x86_64` ABI with official Khronos validation-layer `jniLibs`, `AndroidAbi` / Gradle `mirakanai.androidAbi` ABI matching, APK-packaged `lib/x86_64/libVkLayer_khronos_validation.so`, `VK_LAYER_KHRONOS_validation` enumeration, clean logcat validation output, and offscreen Vulkan readback. `tools/validate-environment-highest-commercial-readiness.ps1 -RequireReady` now reports `environment_highest_commercial_ready=1`, `environment_commercial_ready=1`, 16 ready rows, 0 host-gated/dependency-gated/blocked/unsupported/missing rows, 21 retained optimization workload/backend rows, and `environment_all_platform_unconditional_ready=1`. Broad `environment_ready` remains intentionally unclaimed at 0.

Current production-completion state: `engine/agent/manifest.json.aiOperableProductionLoop.currentActivePlan` points at `docs/superpowers/master-plans/2026-05-03-production-completion-master-plan-v1.md`; `recommendedNextPlan.id = next-production-gap-selection`; `unsupportedProductionGaps = []`. Diagnostics Backend Adapter Handoff v1 (`diagnostics-backend-adapter-handoff-v1`) is completed retained clean-break evidence for dependency-free crash/telemetry handoff: `DiagnosticsOpsPlanOptions` uses `DiagnosticsCrashReviewAdapterDesc`, `DiagnosticsTelemetryBackendDesc`, and `DiagnosticsOpsAdapterDesc`; `build_diagnostics_ops_plan` keeps telemetry `unsupported` without a backend descriptor, marks partial descriptors `host_gated`, and reports ready only after backend id, producer, OpenTelemetry resource `service.name`, `resourceSpans` trace contract review, local path redaction, secret redaction, and operator handoff evidence are present. Crash review similarly requires Debugging Tools for Windows, symbol configuration, dump capture policy review, and operator handoff evidence. This does not add native dump writing, debugger execution, telemetry SDK/upload execution, network dependencies, symbol publication, native handles, or external-engine compatibility/parity/equivalence claims. Renderer Commercial Readiness Evidence Promotion v1 (`renderer-commercial-readiness-evidence-promotion-v1`) is retained as host-gated evidence rather than a completed ready claim. It implemented the retained `GameEngine.RendererCommercialReadinessEvidence.v1` artifact contract, official-source rows, value-only promotion planning, package-visible evidence, clean-room/legal proof, non-promoting producer/importer/assembler/handoff tools, current-run intake, run discovery, and public runner security review gate. 2026-06-30 live evidence after PR #915 / merge commit `38e68e281efa82d99b91fe606c665e4bc7f347be` reports source run `28450893645`, no `renderer-metal-memory-profiling-host-artifacts` run, no idle online `self-hosted, macOS, ARM64, metal-residency-set` runner, final handoff `capable_host_runner_required` / `provision_capable_host_runner`, valid retained public-runner security review, and `renderer_commercial_readiness=0`. Renderer Commercial Quality Closeout v1 (`renderer-commercial-quality-closeout-v1`, `docs/superpowers/plans/2026-06-25-renderer-commercial-quality-closeout-v1.md`) remains completed retained fail-closed evidence, with broad renderer claims blocked until exact retained non-fixture evidence passes final promotion. Broad all-feature/all-platform 2D engine readiness, broad editor execution, embedded runtime-host playtest, package scripts, arbitrary shell, broad hot reload productization, backend parity, Metal readiness, renderer/RHI ownership, external-engine parity, and broad `environment_ready` remain unclaimed.

2D Source Pulse Package Smoke v1 remains retained selected package-visible evidence for Original 2D Commercial Authoring Live Iteration v1: `installed-2d-source-pulse-smoke` / `--require-2d-source-pulse` reports `2d_source_pulse_status=ready` with reviewed change rows and runtime replacement safe-point proof. Source Pulse does not import Unity, Unreal Engine, or Godot projects, schemas, code, samples, assets, or UI; legal readiness remains an engineering evidence gate, not legal advice or legal clearance automation.

2D Commercial Authoring Review Models v1 adds `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewStatus`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewSurface`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewRowInput`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewRow`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewDesc`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringReviewModel`, `make_editor_2d_commercial_authoring_review_model`, and `make_editor_2d_commercial_authoring_review_ui_model` in `MK_editor_core`. The model aggregates retained first-party atlas inspection, tile-set review, tilemap chunk editing, collision overlay review, animation preview, package-diff review, and validation diagnostics rows from existing sprite/tilemap/preflight diagnostics plus explicit tile-set/package-diff review inputs. It is value-only and fail-closed for missing retained rows, duplicate retained ids, input mutation/execution/native-handle claims, package mutation, validation execution, runtime source parsing, renderer/RHI handle exposure, external engine project import, and external engine API parity claims. This is not visible editor productization, package mutation application, runtime-host playtest, source parser promotion, broad commercial 2D readiness, external engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

2D Commercial Package Update Review Models v1 adds `Editor2DCommercialPackageUpdateReviewStatus`, `Editor2DCommercialPackageSmokeReviewStatus`, `Editor2DCommercialPackageUpdateReviewDesc`, `Editor2DCommercialPackageUpdateReviewModel`, `make_editor_2d_commercial_package_update_review_model`, `make_editor_2d_commercial_package_update_review_ui_model`, and `make_editor_2d_commercial_package_update_apply_action` in `MK_editor_core`. The review model gates reviewed `runtimePackageFiles` updates with manifest revision checks, undo/redo action readiness, safe mutation preview rows, selected package smoke evidence, rejection diagnostics, and fail-closed unsupported-claim diagnostics before creating an undoable apply action. The action reuses the existing narrow `ScenePackageRegistrationApplyPlan` / `apply_scene_package_registration_to_manifest` path and can be executed through `UndoStack` to redo/undo the reviewed manifest text update. It does not execute validation recipes, package scripts, shell commands, runtime source parsing, external engine project import, native-handle exposure, visible editor widgets, broad package mutation workflows, broad commercial 2D readiness, external engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

2D Commercial Large-Scene Asset Navigation v1 adds `ContentBrowserNavigationAction`, `ContentBrowserNavigationRequest`, `ContentBrowserNavigationRow`, `ContentBrowserNavigationModel`, `kContentBrowserNavigationMaxPageSize`, and `plan_content_browser_navigation` in `MK_editor_core`. The value-only planner pages the existing filtered `ContentBrowserState` result set, clamps unsafe page sizes and offsets, locates the selected visible asset, exposes first/previous/next/last/selected-page navigation state, and reports diagnostics without mutating browser state or executing import tools. This is an editor-core primitive for large asset browser/import flows; it is not visible shell productization, asset import execution, package mutation, runtime package streaming, external engine project import, native-handle exposure, broad commercial 2D readiness, external engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

2D Commercial Authoring Workflow Proof v1 adds `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofStatus`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofSourceOrigin`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofSourceRowInput`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofSourceRow`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofDesc`, `Editor2DCommercialAuthoringWorkflowProofModel`, `make_editor_2d_commercial_authoring_workflow_proof_model`, and `make_editor_2d_commercial_authoring_workflow_proof_ui_model` in `MK_editor_core`. The value-only proof aggregates the existing 2D commercial authoring review, package update review, large-scene asset navigation, and `review_production_authoring_workflow` result, then requires source rows to be either first-party sample content or generated fixtures before reporting accepted workflow, mutation-ledger, validation-repair, and navigation counters. It fails closed for external assets, external engine project/schema rows, copied material, command execution, file mutation, package IO, runtime source parsing, native-handle exposure, external engine API parity, and legal-approval claims. This is retained engineering evidence only; it is not autonomous content generation, visible editor productization, package-script execution, external engine import, broad commercial 2D readiness, external engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

2D Commercial Package Residency Policy v1 adds `RuntimePackageResidencyPolicyStatus`, `RuntimePackageResidencyTelemetryRow`, `RuntimePackageResidencyPolicyDesc`, `RuntimePackageResidencyPolicyPlan`, and `plan_runtime_package_residency_policy` in `MK_runtime`. The value-only planner reviews all already-mounted cooked packages, including overlay-overridden resident payloads, reports resident byte/record/package counters, caller-supplied IO, decompressed-byte, decompression-time, CPU-time, GPU-upload, memory high-water, asset-miss, and pop-in telemetry, LRU candidate order from reviewed `last_touched_frame` rows, protected eviction blockers, and recommended eviction mount ids without mutating live residency. It saturates aggregate counters at numeric limits, records memory high-water as a maximum, and fails closed for ambiguous telemetry, unsupported execution requests, and explicit aggregate telemetry budget overages. It does not read package files, launch background IO, execute package scripts, spawn external processes, parse runtime source assets, touch renderer/RHI residency, expose native handles, prove broad background streaming, long-run performance readiness, broad commercial 2D readiness, external-engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

2D Commercial Package Background Read Queue v1 adds `RuntimePackageBackgroundReadQueueDesc`, `RuntimePackageBackgroundLoadedRow`, `RuntimePackageBackgroundReadQueueResult`, `RuntimePackageBackgroundReadServiceState`, `RuntimePackageBackgroundReadServiceTickDesc`, `RuntimePackageBackgroundReadServiceTickResult`, `dispatch_runtime_package_background_reads`, and `tick_runtime_package_background_read_service` in `MK_runtime`. The queue validates reviewed `RuntimePackageStreamingExecutionDesc` rows, dispatches only package candidate loads through caller-owned `JobExecutionPool` workers, preserves deterministic input-order loaded rows, and lets the service retain pending rows, coalesce duplicate target/package descriptors, and dispatch bounded rows across ticks. Loaded rows are for later caller-owned safe-point adoption through existing package streaming safe-point APIs. This does not mount packages, mutate resident sets, refresh catalogs, execute package scripts, spawn external processes, parse runtime source assets, touch renderer/RHI residency, expose native handles, execute DirectStorage, prove async-overlap/performance, promote broad background package streaming, broad commercial 2D readiness, external-engine compatibility/equivalence/parity/replacement/endorsement, or legal approval.

Renderer Commercial Readiness Evidence Promotion v1 Task 1 adds the retained `GameEngine.RendererCommercialReadinessEvidence.v1` bundle contract through `schemas/renderer-commercial-readiness-evidence.schema.json` plus ready, missing Metal, and external-engine rejected fixtures. It records D3D12, strict Vulkan, Apple-host Metal, renderer quality matrix, production VFX/profiling, Metal memory/profiling, selected 3D/UI/environment/generated-game package evidence, and third-party notice rows while preserving clean-room legal review for Unity, Unreal Engine, and Godot. The contract is MIRAIKANAI-specific and rejects external engine source, sample code, shader code, UI expression, assets, trademarks, compatibility claims, equivalence claims, and parity claims.

Renderer Commercial Readiness Evidence Promotion v1 Task 2 adds `RendererCommercialReadinessSourceRow`, `RendererCommercialReadinessEvidenceRow`, `RendererCommercialReadinessPromotionDesc`, `RendererCommercialReadinessPromotionPlan`, and `plan_renderer_commercial_readiness_promotion` in `MK_renderer`. The value-only promotion layer consumes the ready quality closeout plan plus retained source, artifact hash, validation recipe, package counter, clean-room, notice, and legal rows; it never executes GPU commands, native captures, shell commands, package scripts, crash uploads, or network requests, never exposes native handles, and rejects cross-backend Metal inference plus Unity/Unreal Engine/Godot compatibility, equivalence, parity, code, sample, asset, trademark, UI expression, or API rows before `renderer_commercial_readiness` can become true.

Renderer Commercial Readiness Evidence Promotion v1 Tasks 3-10AN add `tools/validate-renderer-commercial-readiness-evidence.ps1`, `tools/collect-renderer-commercial-readiness-evidence.ps1`, current-run CI artifact intake, and exact retained artifact checks for D3D12 command allocator/fence, resource barriers, timestamps, debug validation, residency, package readback, and native-handle non-exposure; strict Vulkan synchronization2, validation layer, synchronization validation, memory binding, timestamp, SPIR-V validation, package readback, and native-handle non-exposure; Apple Metal `metal`/`metallib`, MSL address/resource/stage proof, visible package rows, and cross-backend non-inference; separate Metal memory/profiling `MTLHeap`, `MTLResidencySet`, and `MTLCaptureManager` evidence; full retained `GameEngine.RendererMetalMemoryProfilingHostEvidence.v1` imports for `memory_residency` and `profiling_capture`; package-visible 3D/UI/environment/generated-game rows; and clean-room/legal zero rows for external-engine code, samples, shaders, UI expression, assets, trademarks, project import, API use, compatibility, equivalence, and parity claims. Task 10AB keeps Vulkan 1.3 synchronization2 as the selected contract while resolving the official `VK_KHR_synchronization2` aliases for `vkCmdPipelineBarrier2`, `vkQueueSubmit2`, and `vkCmdWriteTimestamp2` when hosted drivers expose KHR entry point names; this enables real timestamp-query execution without broadening readiness or exposing native handles. Task 10AD lets hosted strict Vulkan collection retain either ready timestamp evidence or a fail-closed host-gated summary while preserving `renderer_commercial_readiness=0` until final retained-root promotion. Task 10AE maps hosted `tools/validate-renderer-metal-apple.ps1` source/toolchain/MSL/visible-package rows into the exact Apple Metal commercial host-evidence producer input, including a deterministic visible-package SHA-256, while keeping Metal memory/profiling separate and all broad renderer counters at `0`. Task 10AH lets the final artifact importer download named supplemental run artifacts such as `renderer-metal-memory-profiling-host-artifacts` through `-SupplementalRunIds` / `-SupplementalArtifactNames` and opt in to regenerate quality/VFX host evidence through `-RegenerateQualityVfx` once package, D3D12, strict Vulkan, Apple Metal, Metal memory/profiling, and generated-3D rows are present. Task 10AI adds `.github/workflows/renderer-commercial-readiness-final-from-runs.yml` / `renderer-commercial-readiness-final-from-runs` as the manual handoff from `source_artifact_run_id` plus `metal_memory_profiling_run_id` into `renderer-commercial-readiness-final-from-runs-artifact-intake`; it passes `RegenerateQualityVfx` and `AutoAssemble` through the importer while keeping `renderer_commercial_readiness=0`. Task 10AJ adds `tools/validate-renderer-metal-memory-profiling-capable-host-runner.ps1` as the capable-host runner preflight that calls GitHub CLI `gh api` for `/repos/{owner}/{repo}/actions/runners` and requires an idle online runner labelled `self-hosted, macOS, ARM64, metal-residency-set` before dispatching the Metal memory/profiling supplemental workflow; current 2026-06-27 audit evidence for `y2ikgm89/mirakanai-engine` reports `renderer_metal_memory_profiling_capable_host_runner_available=0` and `renderer_metal_memory_profiling_capable_host_runner_total=0`, so this remains host-gated and non-promoting. Task 10AL adds `renderer-public-runner-security-review`, `rendererPublicRunnerSecurityReviewGenerator`, `tools/generate-renderer-public-runner-security-review.ps1`, and `tools/check-renderer-public-runner-security-review.ps1` as the retained public repository security review artifact producer for self-hosted runner provisioning. It reads repository metadata through `GET /repos/{owner}/{repo}` or `-RepositoryJsonPath`, requires `-ApprovePublicRepoSelfHostedRunnerReview public-repo-self-hosted-runner-risk-reviewed`, `-ReviewedPublicForkPrRisk`, `-ReviewedRunnerIsolation`, `-ReviewedSecretExposure`, and `-ReviewedMetalProbeTruth`, writes `GameEngine.RendererPublicSelfHostedRunnerSecurityReview.v1` only with `review_status=approved`, `reviewed_public_fork_pr_risk`, `reviewed_runner_isolation`, `reviewed_secret_exposure`, `reviewed_allowed_workflows`, exact `reviewed_required_labels` `self-hosted, macOS, ARM64, metal-residency-set`, and `reviewed_metal_probe_truth`, then feeds `-PublicRepoRunnerSecurityReviewRelative` for final handoff rows such as `runner_public_repo_security_review_artifact_present`, `runner_public_repo_security_review_artifact_valid`, and `runner_public_repo_security_review_artifact_status`. Missing review emits `renderer_public_runner_security_review` blockers and preserves `complete_public_runner_security_review`; approved review records the official `/repos/{owner}/{repo}/actions/runners/registration-token` endpoint, that the registration token expires after one hour, and Metal probe truth without fetching/printing tokens, registering runners, dispatching workflows, or running GPU work. Task 10AM adds `renderer-commercial-readiness-final-run-discovery`, `rendererCommercialReadinessFinalRunDiscovery`, `tools/plan-renderer-commercial-readiness-final-run-discovery.ps1`, and `tools/check-renderer-commercial-readiness-final-run-discovery.ps1` as a plan-only GitHub Actions run/artifact discovery layer. It reads `GET /repos/{owner}/{repo}/actions/runs` and `GET /repos/{owner}/{repo}/actions/runs/{run_id}/artifacts` through `gh api` or fixture JSON, verifies `renderer-commercial-readiness-current-run-artifact-intake` and `renderer-metal-memory-profiling-host-artifacts`, then prints the exact `gh workflow run renderer-commercial-readiness-final-from-runs.yml` handoff only when both IDs are present. Task 10AN extends final handoff fail-closed behavior so a known public repository with an already online matching self-hosted runner still withholds `gh workflow run renderer-metal-memory-profiling-capable-host.yml` until the public runner security review is confirmed. It never dispatches workflows, downloads artifacts, fetches registration tokens, registers runners, runs GPU workloads, assembles evidence, or promotes readiness. The collector assembles already-collected non-fixture host artifacts into `artifacts/renderer/commercial-readiness-evidence/<retained-artifact-root>/evidence.json`, computes hash rows, copies nested Metal capture artifacts, and emits no readiness promotion by itself. The ready fixture can mark the four final renderer closeout counters ready only for fixture artifacts; copied fixture artifacts under a retained `artifacts/renderer/commercial-readiness-evidence/...` root are rejected by `tools/check-renderer-commercial-readiness-evidence-fixture-guard.ps1` with `fixture_artifact_rejected`; full retained Metal memory/profiling evidence can promote only `renderer_metal_memory_profiling_ready`; default validation without a retained artifact root still emits all four counters as `0` and keeps `renderer_environment_ready=0`.

Task 10 remains open only for final non-fixture row promotion. The D3D12, strict Vulkan, Apple-host Metal, package-visible, renderer-quality-matrix, production VFX/profiling, clean-room/legal retained commercial artifact producers, Task 10F final promotion preflight, final retained-root assembler, Metal-host CI retained-root artifact upload hook, and GitHub Actions artifact intake now exist as non-promoting shapers/checks, each with a separate static check and manifest recipe or workflow guard. The selected `linux-vulkan` lane now runs the supported Linux package presentation/readback/clean-log smoke with `--emit-vulkan-strict-commercial-host-gate`, then uploads `renderer-vulkan-strict-commercial-quality-host-evidence` as a fail-closed `host_evidence_required` summary from `tools/generate-renderer-vulkan-strict-commercial-quality-host-evidence.ps1`; `games/sample_desktop_runtime_game/linux_main.cpp` accepts the future strict aggregate, GPU memory, and debug profiling `--require-*` flags but fails them until real execution rows exist. Platform-only `linux-vulkan-host-evidence` remains insufficient for `vulkan_strict_host_evidence`, and ready non-fixture strict Vulkan retained JSON still requires a future strict Linux package log with aggregate, GPU memory, and debug profiling counters after core/KHR synchronization2 command resolution has produced positive timestamp frequency/write/read counters. The macOS Metal lane retains `renderer-apple-metal-commercial-quality-host-evidence` separately from `renderer-metal-memory-profiling-host-artifacts`, so Apple-host commercial rows and Metal memory/profiling rows remain separate final assembler sources. The package producer shapes selected visible 3D, runtime UI, environment package-consumption, and generated-game rows into the four package artifacts without package-script execution, native handles, external-engine parity, or broad `environment_ready`. The quality/VFX producer shapes retained `renderer-quality-matrix.json` and `production-vfx-profiling.json` rows with `renderer_quality_matrix_status=host_evidence_required`, deterministic replay hashes, clean diagnostics, and zero GPU command/native capture/crash-upload side effects. The clean-room/legal producer shapes official public Unity, Unreal Engine, and Godot legal/trademark/license category review into `clean-room-legal.json`, rejects fixture inputs and unsafe paths, keeps any external-engine code/sample/shader/UI expression/asset/trademark/project/API/compatibility/equivalence/parity row at `renderer_clean_room_legal_ready=0`, and adds no dependency, copied material, or distributable third-party asset. `tools/assemble-renderer-commercial-readiness-final-retained-root.ps1` requires seven explicit host/package/legal inputs, stages producer outputs under `_producer-artifacts`, assembles the final retained root, and then runs the final preflight; it does not run GPU work or promote readiness by itself. `tools/import-renderer-commercial-readiness-final-retained-root-artifacts.ps1` records `workflow_artifact_list`, `artifact_handoff_strategy`, `supplemental_import`, `missing_assembler_inputs`, `assembler_handoff`, `final_preflight_handoff`, and `quality_vfx_regenerate` rows in its intake manifest so downloaded artifact inputs can be handed to the final assembler or preflight without manual path inference; it separates optional final retained-root artifact availability from assembler source artifact availability, emits exact missing assembler input names, can merge explicitly named supplemental run artifacts, can regenerate quality/VFX host evidence only when all source rows are present, and keeps all broad renderer counters at `0`. Its validation-recipe DryRun uses `-Mode Plan` and never requires `RunId`, downloads artifacts, regenerates quality/VFX evidence, or passes `-RequireReady`. `validate.yml` uploads `artifacts/renderer/commercial-readiness-evidence/final-retained/**` from the Metal host lane as `renderer-commercial-readiness-final-retained-root` only when such files exist, using `if-no-files-found: warn` and without generating evidence. The `renderer-commercial-artifact-intake` job captures the current workflow run artifact list, invokes the importer in `Import` mode with `github.run_id` / `github.repository`, confirms `renderer_commercial_readiness=0`, and uploads `renderer-commercial-readiness-current-run-artifact-intake` so artifact availability, download failures, assembler inputs, and final-preflight handoff are retained without manual path inference. The hosted Metal optimization producer now bounds `xcrun xctrace record` with official `--time-limit` through default `XctraceTimeLimit=10m`, adds a host-level `XctraceRecordTimeoutSeconds=900` watchdog, emits `xctrace_time_limit=10m`, `xctrace_record_timeout_seconds=900`, and `xctrace_record_watchdog_timeout`, and only tolerates a watchdog timeout when the trace still exports through `xctrace export --toc` and `tools/validate-environment-optimization-artifacts.ps1 -RequireReady` passes. `tools/validate-renderer-commercial-readiness-final-promotion-preflight.ps1` checks the selected final retained root for 12 required files, copied fixture artifacts, full Metal memory/profiling host evidence, clean-room legal evidence, schema/claim/recipe mismatches, and downstream validator readiness while keeping all broad renderer counters at `0` until the real retained root validates. The remaining implementation order is real host artifact capture and final non-fixture `-RequireReady` promotion. Each producer must fail closed, emit `fixture_only=false` only from retained first-party host/package/legal evidence, and leave `renderer_commercial_readiness=0` until every selected backend, package, quality, Metal memory/profiling, and legal row validates together.

The current artifact intake manifest also records `assembler_input_blockers` rows for host-gated missing assembler inputs, including retained `host_gate_summary_paths`, exact `host_gate_reasons`, and `dependent_missing_inputs`. Its counters include `host_gate_blocked_assembler_inputs`, `host_gate_blocked_assembler_input_names`, and `quality_vfx_dependency_blockers`, so the current hosted chain reports `quality_vfx_host_evidence` as blocked by missing `metal_memory_profiling_host_evidence` rather than flattening both rows into unrelated missing inputs.

`2D Originality Review v1` adds the first Source Pulse clean-room gate in `MK_tools`: `TwoDOriginalitySourceRow`, `TwoDOriginalityDiagnostic`, `TwoDOriginalityReviewResult`, and `review_2d_originality_sources` accept first-party design, official documentation category, official platform SDK, and permissive notice rows while rejecting copied code/assets/documentation, external engine schemas, trademark surfaces, and external engine compatibility/equivalence/parity claims. `review_2d_commercial_production_sources` layers a stricter commercial production source gate over the same rows, requiring first-party design, official documentation category, and official platform/SDK source rows before `official_source_ledger_ready` and `commercial_production_source_gate_ready` can become ready. The result remains value-only and counsel-review-required; it does not execute package mutation, command execution, native handles, Source Pulse watch bridging, runtime active-session replacement, package-visible smoke counters, legal conclusions, or legal clearance automation.

`2D Commercial Clean-Room Source Ledger v1` adds `docs/specs/2026-06-30-2d-commercial-clean-room-source-ledger-v1.md`, `tools/check-2d-commercial-clean-room.ps1`, `tools/check-2d-commercial-clean-room-contract.ps1`, `tools/check-2d-commercial-source-diagnostics.ps1`, `tools/check-2d-commercial-source-diagnostics-contract.ps1`, `tools/generate-2d-commercial-clean-room-review-input.ps1`, `schemas/2d-commercial-clean-room-review-input.schema.json`, and `schemas/2d-commercial-official-source-summary.schema.json`. The guards scan public engine headers, game code/manifests, editor-core public headers, and selected schemas for prohibited external-engine public tokens, explicit copied-material markers, external schema/project markers, trademark public-surface markers, missing-notice markers, unapproved-dependency markers, or compatibility/equivalence/parity/importer claims; successful diagnostics output is scoped to `retained_markers_and_public_surface_tokens`. The generator emits official-source rows, separate Context7 reference mirror rows, and counsel-review input without drawing legal conclusions while preserving `2d_commercial_clean_room_commercial_ready=0` and `2d_commercial_clean_room_legal_approval=0`. This adds no dependency, no copied external-engine code/sample/shader/UI expression/asset/schema/API surface, and no Unity/Unreal Engine/Godot/GameMaker/Defold/O3DE compatibility, equivalence, parity, project-import, replacement, or legal-approval claim.

`2D Commercial Large-Project Fixtures v1` adds `aiWorkflow.twoDCommercialLargeProjectFixtures` / `2d-commercial-large-project-fixtures-v1` to the selected `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` manifest and schema, guarded by `tools/check-json-contracts-080-2d-commercial-large-project-fixtures.ps1`. It records stable output under many assets, duplicate names, missing dependencies, invalid metadata, and asset deletion/rename churn by linking source manifests, deterministic cook outputs, production atlas packing, runtime source parser exclusion, runtime package files, fail-closed diagnostics, and equal baseline/post-churn replay hashes. This is retained first-party fixture evidence only; runtime source parsing, external asset ingestion, package scripts, renderer/RHI residency, broad large-project readiness, broad commercial 2D readiness, compatibility/equivalence/parity, and legal approval remain unclaimed.

`2D Source Pulse Watch Bridge v1` adds `TwoDSourcePulseDesc`, `TwoDSourcePulseEventRow`, `TwoDSourcePulsePlan`, `TwoDSourcePulseStatus`, and `plan_2d_source_pulse_events` in `MK_tools` to convert caller-supplied `FileWatchEvent` value rows into Source Pulse rows over `AssetHotReloadEventKind`. It rejects unknown events, invalid paths, native handles, autonomous background commits, package scripts, and renderer/RHI requests. It does not construct or own platform watchers, execute recook, mutate packages, commit runtime replacements, expose active-session hot reload, or independently claim package-visible counters outside the selected Source Pulse package smoke lane.

`2D Source Pulse Runtime Replacement v1` adds `TwoDSourcePulseRuntimeReplacementDesc`, `TwoDSourcePulseRuntimeReplacementResult`, and `execute_2d_source_pulse_runtime_replacement_safe_point` in `MK_tools` to promote already-reviewed asset-aware Source Pulse rows into the existing registered asset watch tick and reviewed runtime package replacement safe point. It requires runtime scene validation, operator safe-point review, and `source_pulse.safe_point_required=true`, rejects editor-core execution, arbitrary shell execution, native handle exposure, and active-session replacement without a safe point, and preserves existing recook/runtime replacement failure diagnostics. It does not construct platform watchers, execute package scripts, expose native handles, infer broad active-session hot reload readiness, or independently claim package-visible counters outside the selected Source Pulse package smoke lane.

`2D Live Iteration Review Model v1` adds `Editor2DLiveIterationEvidenceRow`, `Editor2DLiveIterationReviewDesc`, `Editor2DLiveIterationReviewModel`, `make_editor_2d_live_iteration_review_model`, and `make_editor_2d_live_iteration_review_ui_model` in `MK_editor_core` to project originality, runtime scene validation, Source Pulse watch bridge, package replacement safe-point, and external evidence rows into retained `2d_live_iteration.review.*` UI ids. Stale revisions, native handles, shell/process execution, validation-recipe execution, screen coordinates, target mismatches, missing confirmation, unsupported parameters, disabled commands, and unknown command ids fail closed in editor core.

Phase 9 of the completed plan locks cross-platform UI/editor adapters as future gates rather than readiness claims. Durable future-gate row names are `editor.cross_platform.adapter.macos.core_text`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.macos.input_method_kit`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.macos.nsaccessibility`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.linux.at_spi`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.linux.ibus`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.linux.fcitx`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.android.input_method_service`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.android.accessibility`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.ios.uitextinput`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.ios.uiaccessibility`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.dependency.harfbuzz`, `editor.cross_platform.adapter.dependency.freetype`, and `editor.cross_platform.adapter.dependency.icu`; every one remains host-gated or dependency-gated. Windows DirectWrite/TSF/UIA evidence must not be read as Core Text/InputMethodKit/NSAccessibility, AT-SPI/IBus/Fcitx, Android InputMethodService/accessibility, iOS UITextInput/UIAccessibility, HarfBuzz, FreeType, or ICU readiness. Generated games and runtime UI remain on public `mirakana::ui` contracts and must not depend on editor-private APIs. Any future third-party text/font/image dependency still requires `license-audit`, `vcpkg.json`, `docs/dependencies.md`, and `THIRD_PARTY_NOTICES.md` before use.

Source Pulse Import Duplicate Review v1 adds value-only collision review to the existing asset import candidate pipeline. `review_editor_asset_import_candidates` now blocks duplicate source paths, duplicate output/imported paths, duplicate `AssetKeyV2` values, and duplicate content hashes before registration/import planning, exposes review-only deterministic `<stem>_2` through `<stem>_99` rename suggestions for output/key/imported-path collisions, validates selected alternate paths by kind and imported-output root, and allows content-hash reuse only for one unambiguous existing source with matching provenance and explicit `reuse_existing_source`. It does not copy files, overwrite existing project paths, write `GameEngine.SourceAssetRegistry.v1`, execute importers, parse runtime source assets, expose native handles, or claim Unity/Unreal/Godot compatibility.

## Ready Foundations

- Generic 2D Sandbox Tile Simulation Primitives v1 adds `RuntimeSandboxTileMaterialRow`, `RuntimeSandboxTileSimulationDesc`, `RuntimeSandboxTileSimulationPlan`, `RuntimeSandboxTileCollisionSpanRow`, `RuntimeSandboxTileCellRow`, `RuntimeSandboxLightPropagationRow`, `RuntimeSandboxLiquidFlowRow`, `RuntimeSandboxScheduledTileUpdateRow`, and `plan_runtime_sandbox_tile_simulation` in `MK_runtime` so already-reviewed runtime sandbox worlds can produce deterministic tile collision, platform, liquid, trigger, light-propagation, and scheduled-update rows with replay hashes and explicit zero physics/renderer/platform/thread side-effect flags. This is unit-tested in `MK_runtime_sandbox_world_runtime_tests`; it does not upload physics shapes, write lightmaps, run full fluid simulation, call renderer/platform APIs, create threads, load packages, write persistence, or encode game-specific biome/block-art rules.
- Generic 2D Sandbox Persistence Snapshot v1 adds `RuntimeSandboxWorldPersistenceDocumentDesc`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldPersistenceDocumentPlan`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldSnapshotDiffDesc`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldMigrationReviewPlan`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldAtomicSavePlan`, `plan_runtime_sandbox_world_persistence_document`, `plan_runtime_sandbox_world_snapshot_diff`, `review_runtime_sandbox_world_migration`, and `plan_runtime_sandbox_world_atomic_save` in `MK_runtime` so already-built runtime sandbox worlds can produce canonical snapshot text, chunk/layer/changed-cell rows, deterministic content hashes, dirty-chunk diff rows, schema migration/recovery review rows, and atomic-save operation intent rows. This is unit-tested in `MK_runtime_sandbox_world_persistence_tests`; it plans safe rooted project-relative temp/target/backup paths and flush/replace/rollback intent, but it does not write files, call Win32, invoke `IFileSystem`, mutate packages, execute migration steps, create threads, or expose native handles.
- Generic 2D Sandbox Streaming Residency v1 adds `RuntimeSandboxWorldStreamingPlan`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldStreamingSourceRow`, `RuntimeSandboxWorldAddressableDependencyRow`, `plan_runtime_sandbox_world_streaming`, and `execute_runtime_sandbox_world_streaming_safe_point` in `MK_runtime` so already-built runtime sandbox worlds can review source-range chunk selection, dirty resident chunk pinning, addressable tile-atlas/biome-material/audio/prefab dependencies, world-region residency budgets, and a host safe-point adoption path over reviewed package candidates. This is unit-tested in `MK_runtime_sandbox_world_streaming_tests` together with the existing world-region and addressable streaming suites; it does not create background threads, run async addressable execution, invoke automatic LRU eviction, expose native handles, upload renderer/RHI resources, implement broad package streaming, or encode game-specific biome/block-art rules.
- Generic 2D Sandbox Production Tile Renderer v1 adds `TileChunkCellRow`, `TileChunkDirtyRegion`, `TileChunkLightCellRow`, `TileChunkRendererDesc`, `TileChunkRendererPlan`, `TileChunkSpriteRow`, `TileChunkDrawRow`, `TileChunkDirtyRebuildRow`, `TileChunkLightmapRow`, and `plan_tile_chunk_renderer` in `MK_renderer` so reviewed tile chunks can produce deterministic sprite rows, opaque/transparent draw grouping, dirty rebuild budget rows, and renderer-neutral lightmap rows. This is unit-tested in `MK_renderer_tile_chunk_renderer_tests`; `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package --require-production-tile-renderer` reports `tile_chunk_renderer_*` counters for visible/opaque/transparent cells, sprite/draw rows, texture binds, dirty rebuild rows/cells, light rows, changed light cells, clean diagnostics, and zero backend submission/native texture ownership invocation. It does not create backend-native texture ownership, backend-specific submission, runtime renderer/RHI residency, public native handles, SDL3, or broad renderer-quality claims.
- Generic 2D Sandbox Authoring Review v1 adds `SandboxWorldAuthoringPackageDesc`, `SandboxWorldTileDefinitionRow`, `SandboxWorldPaletteBrushRow`, `SandboxWorldChunkTemplateRow`, `SandboxWorldProceduralSeedRow`, `sandbox_world_authoring_review_format_v1`, `review_sandbox_world_authoring_package`, and `apply_sandbox_world_authoring_package` in `MK_tools` so reviewed tile definitions, palette brushes, chunk templates, procedural seeds, changed files, tilemap package changed-file rows, and dependency edges can be validated and applied through safe package-relative paths. This is unit-tested in `MK_tools_sandbox_world_authoring_tests`; `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package --require-sandbox-authoring-review` reports `sandbox_authoring_review_*` counters and zero external image decoding, external download, importer plugin, package apply during review, and diagnostic counters. It does not parse runtime source assets, decode external images, download content, execute importer plugins, mutate packages during review, create renderer/RHI residency, expose native handles, or claim full tilemap editor productization.
- Generic 2D Sandbox Gameplay Integration Rows v1 adds `RuntimeSandboxDayNightPhase`, `RuntimeSandboxTriggerKind`, `RuntimeSandboxTileDropRow`, `RuntimeSandboxConstructionCostConsumptionRow`, `RuntimeSandboxToolEffectivenessRow`, `RuntimeSandboxSpawnRegionRow`, `RuntimeSandboxDayNightEventRow`, and `RuntimeSandboxTriggerRow` to `plan_runtime_sandbox_world_mutation` in `MK_runtime` so mutable sandbox worlds can expose generic tile-drop, construction-cost consumption, tool-effectiveness, spawn-region, day/night event, and trigger rows for game-owned inventory, crafting, quest/dialogue, AI, perception, spawning, and interaction systems. This is unit-tested in `MK_runtime_genre_sandbox_world_tests`; `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` reports `sandbox_world_cost_consumption_rows=1`, `sandbox_world_tile_drop_rows=1`, `sandbox_world_tool_effectiveness_rows=1`, `sandbox_world_spawn_region_rows=1`, `sandbox_world_day_night_event_rows=1`, and `sandbox_world_trigger_rows=1`. It rejects boss/NPC catalogs, hardcoded damage formula ids, economy/price/currency balance hooks, backend/native/editor/RHI/package terms, and game-owned content rules; it does not execute game rules, mutate inventory, spawn actors, run dialogue, own balance, write persistence, call renderer/platform/editor APIs, expose native handles, or reintroduce SDL3.
- Sandbox World Network And Modding Gate v1 adds `RuntimeNetworkSandboxMutationCommandRow`, `RuntimeNetworkSandboxSnapshotDeltaRow`, `RuntimeScriptModdingAdapterPolicyRow`, `RuntimeScriptModdingDeniedCapabilityRow`, `plan_runtime_network_replication` sandbox row review, and `plan_runtime_script_modding_policy` in `MK_runtime` so sandbox-world mutation input and snapshot delta evidence plus modding adapter metadata can be reviewed as deterministic value rows. This is unit-tested in `MK_runtime_production_network_replication_tests` and `MK_runtime_scripting_sandbox_tests`; it validates sandbox command authority, unique command ids, sequence uniqueness, monotonic ticks, delta command references, shared snapshot/delta byte budgets, reviewed deterministic mod adapter rows, and denied filesystem/network/process/native-plugin/package-mutation capabilities. It does not open sockets, perform network IO, execute rollback/prediction, mutate worlds, load scripts, parse runtime source, open files, spawn processes, bind native plugins, mutate packages, expose native handles, reintroduce SDL3, or claim broad online multiplayer or broad modding readiness.
- C++23 engine module baseline with explicit ownership boundaries and public `mirakana::` APIs: raw pointers and references are non-owning observers, `std::unique_ptr` is the default heap-ownership transfer type, `std::span` / `std::string_view` are borrowed views, and first-party opaque handles/ids carry stable cross-module references without exposing native backend objects.
- Environment Texture Runtime Payload Ingest and Upload Plan v1 adds `RuntimeEnvironmentTexturePayload`, `runtime_environment_texture_payload`, `RuntimeEnvironmentTexturePayloadUploadPlanResult`, and `plan_runtime_environment_texture_payload_upload` in `MK_runtime` for dependency-free read-only validation and selected upload planning of `GameEngine.EnvironmentTextureGeassetPayload.v1` records. It checks record path, source hash/provenance/license rows, OpenEXR or KTX2/Basis source kind, color/sampler metadata, payload byte count/hash/hex data, recorded official-source cook-stage names, single-mip `rgba8_unorm` upload shape, exact upload byte counts, and fail-closed diagnostics while package diagnostics keep ordinary `GameEngine.CookedTexture.v1` texture validation intact. It does not execute optional codecs, transcode Basis at runtime, call backend APIs, upload GPU textures, prove Vulkan/Metal payload parity by itself, or claim broad asset-pipeline coverage beyond the selected Phase 3 closeout lane.
- Memory Lifetime Taxonomy v1 Phase 2 classifies memory readiness into frame temporary, worker scratch, persistent CPU, package resident CPU, upload/staging, resident GPU, transient GPU, readback, and editor/tooling classes. Existing ready evidence is narrow: runtime resident byte and budget rows, safe-point residency failures, read-only RHI memory diagnostics, upload/staging fences and byte counters, transient alias allocation counters, and selected `gpu_memory_policy_*` package evidence. Global allocator replacement, allocator enforcement, all-core CPU scheduling, NUMA/affinity tuning, broad SIMD quality, automatic/LRU GPU residency, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor parity, cross-backend parity, and broad memory optimization remain unsupported until focused diagnostics and host evidence exist.
- Memory Diagnostics v1 adds the dependency-free `MK_core` data model for `MemoryLifetimeClass`, `MemoryCounterRow`, `MemoryClassDiagnosticsSummary`, `MemoryDiagnosticsSummary`, `MemoryBudgetPressure`, `MemoryDiagnosticsCode`, and `summarize_memory_diagnostics`. It aggregates bytes, allocation counts, reuse counts, reset counts, high-water bytes, class budget pressure, invalid counter rows, stale-generation diagnostics, use-after-safe-point diagnostics, cross-thread-free diagnostics, and false-sharing diagnostics by lifetime class before allocator or scheduler claims. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-memory-diagnostics` now exposes selected package-visible `memory_diagnostics_*` counters for package resident CPU bytes, resident GPU bytes/budget, upload/staging bytes, transient GPU allocation counts, and framegraph aliasing-barrier evidence through `memory_diagnostics_transient_gpu_aliasing_barriers` plus `memory_diagnostics_transient_gpu_framegraph_aliasing_ready` when multi-queue evidence is requested. Allocator hooks/enforcement, automatic/LRU GPU residency, NUMA/affinity, broad SIMD quality, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor parity, cross-backend parity, and broad memory optimization remain follow-up work.
- Frame/Thread Scratch v1 is completed. It provides dependency-free `MK_core` `ScratchArena`, `ScratchLease`, and `ScratchLeaseStatus` APIs for bounded frame temporary and per-worker scratch ownership through non-owning `std::span<std::byte>` leases, non-copyable/non-movable arena owners, deterministic safe-point resets, owner validation, padding-aware high-water counters, cross-thread-free diagnostics, use-after-safe-point diagnostics, and selected package-visible framegraph multi-queue aliasing evidence for transient GPU diagnostic context. Allocator replacement, all-core scheduling, NUMA/affinity tuning, broad SIMD quality, automatic/LRU GPU residency, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor parity, cross-backend parity, and broad memory optimization claims remain unsupported.
- Job Scheduling Evidence v1 is completed. It adds dependency-free `MK_core` value rows, summary APIs, deterministic bounded queue execution evidence, and selected package-visible evidence: `JobWorkerTopologyRow`, `JobQueueCounterRow`, `JobSchedulingWorkItemRow`, `JobSchedulingExecutionOptions`, `JobSchedulingExecutionOrderRow`, `JobSchedulingExecutionEvidence`, `JobSchedulingDiagnosticsSummary`, `JobSchedulingDiagnosticsCode`, `JobSchedulingDiagnosticsStatus`, `summarize_job_scheduling_diagnostics`, `build_job_scheduling_execution_evidence`, `job_scheduling_diagnostics_code_label`, and `job_scheduling_diagnostics_status_label`. These aggregate logical processor count, worker count, queue count, processor-group and NUMA evidence, explicit dependency ids, worker-local output counts, deterministic merge order, submitted/completed jobs, bounded queue capacity, queue high-water, queue overflow, steal attempts/successes, waits, blocked dependencies, dependency cycles, deterministic/non-deterministic merge counts, per-worker `MemoryCounterRow` scratch charges, scratch misuse, undersized batches, and oversized batches before scheduler execution claims. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-job-scheduling-evidence` reports `job_scheduling_evidence_status=ready`, `job_scheduling_evidence_ready=1`, clean diagnostics, two workers, two queue rows, three submitted/completed/executed jobs, three deterministic merges, positive scratch byte/high-water counters, and zero native-thread/thread-pool/affinity/NUMA/SIMD/GPU-overlap side-effect flags. All-core CPU scheduling, thread pools, work stealing execution, affinity pinning, NUMA placement, SMT/hybrid CPU policy, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor parity, cross-backend parity, and broad CPU/GPU/memory optimization claims remain follow-up work.
- Job Execution Worker Pool v1 Phase 2 adds `MK_core` real bounded worker execution plus selected package evidence: `JobExecutionPool`, `JobExecutionPoolDesc`, `JobExecutionBatchDesc`, `JobExecutionTaskDesc`, `JobExecutionContext`, `JobExecutionRunResult`, `JobExecutionPoolStatus`, `JobExecutionRunStatus`, `JobExecutionDiagnosticCode`, `execute(batch)`, `request_stop`, `stop_and_drain`, `worker_threads_started`, and `job_execution_*` label helpers. The pool starts explicit RAII-owned `std::thread` workers, drains each batch before returning, passes worker-local `ScratchArena` and `JobExecutionStopToken` into task bodies, catches task exceptions, rejects invalid tasks/queue overflow/dependency hazards/stopped execution, and returns deterministic `JobSchedulingExecutionEvidence`. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-job-execution-foundation` reports `job_execution_foundation_status=ready`, `job_execution_foundation_ready=1`, two worker threads, three submitted/executed task bodies, three deterministic merges, positive worker scratch byte/high-water counters, and zero work-stealing/affinity/NUMA/SIMD/GPU-overlap/CUDA/HIP/SYCL side-effect counters for the baseline foundation lane. The separate Job Execution Work Stealing v1 slice owns opt-in work stealing; affinity pinning, NUMA placement, SMT/hybrid CPU policy, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor/backend parity, and broad CPU/GPU/memory optimization claims remain follow-up work.
- Job Execution Topology Policy v1 adds portable `MK_core` worker-count selection plus selected package evidence: `JobExecutionTopologyPolicyDesc`, `JobExecutionTopologyPolicy`, `JobExecutionTopologyPolicyStatus`, `JobExecutionTopologyPolicyDiagnosticCode`, `select_job_execution_topology_policy`, `observe_job_execution_logical_processor_count`, and topology policy label helpers. The policy treats `std::thread::hardware_concurrency` as an estimate that can fall back, applies requested-worker, worker-limit, and reserved-logical-processor rules, derives a `JobExecutionPoolDesc`, and reports `host_evidence_required` for missing processor-group or NUMA evidence. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-job-execution-topology-policy` reports `job_execution_topology_policy_status=ready`, `job_execution_topology_policy_ready=1`, `job_execution_topology_policy_observed_logical_processors=8`, `job_execution_topology_policy_effective_logical_processors=8`, `job_execution_topology_policy_selected_worker_count=2`, `job_execution_topology_policy_worker_count_limit=2`, `job_execution_topology_policy_reserved_logical_processors=1`, `job_execution_topology_policy_worker_count_limited_by_cap=1`, and zero processor-group/NUMA/affinity/SIMD/GPU-overlap/CUDA/HIP/SYCL side-effect counters. Affinity pinning, NUMA placement execution, SMT/hybrid CPU policy, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor/backend parity, and broad all-core CPU/GPU/memory optimization claims remain follow-up work.
- Job Execution Work Stealing v1 adds opt-in `MK_core` work stealing on top of `JobExecutionPool`: `JobExecutionPoolDesc::work_stealing_enabled`, `JobExecutionTopologyPolicyDesc::enable_work_stealing`, `JobExecutionTopologyPolicy::work_stealing_applied`, and `JobExecutionRunResult` work-stealing counters expose selected first-party worker-queue stealing without OS affinity or vendor policy. `execute(batch)` preserves drain-before-return and deterministic publish evidence while injecting runtime steal attempt/success/wait counters into `JobSchedulingExecutionEvidence.queue_rows`. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-job-execution-work-stealing` reports `job_execution_work_stealing_status=ready`, `job_execution_work_stealing_ready=1`, two worker threads, two submitted/executed task bodies, two deterministic merges, positive steal attempt/success/wait counters, positive worker scratch byte/high-water counters, `job_execution_work_stealing_applied=1`, and zero affinity/NUMA/SIMD/GPU-overlap/CUDA/HIP/SYCL side-effect counters. Affinity pinning, NUMA placement execution, SMT/hybrid CPU policy, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor/backend parity, and broad all-core CPU/GPU/memory optimization claims remain follow-up work.
- SIMD Dispatch Policy And Evidence v1 plus AVX2 Reviewed Target Execution v1 add narrow `MK_core` scalar/SSE2/AVX2 CPU SIMD dispatch evidence: `CpuSimdFeatureSet`, `CpuSimdLane`, `CpuSimdLaneRequest`, `SimdDispatchPolicyDesc`, `SimdDispatchPolicy`, `SimdDotProductEvidence`, `observe_cpu_simd_features`, `select_simd_dispatch_policy`, `compute_scalar_dot_product`, `build_simd_dot_product_evidence`, and SIMD label helpers. The evidence kernels use borrowed `std::span<const float>` inputs and report a deterministic dot-product result without retaining raw pointers. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-simd-dispatch-policy` reports `simd_dispatch_policy_status=ready`, `simd_dispatch_policy_requested_lane=auto_select`, scalar, SSE2, or AVX2 selected lane, `simd_dispatch_policy_dot_product_result=120`, `simd_dispatch_policy_span_inputs_used=1`, `simd_dispatch_policy_raw_pointers_retained=0`, `simd_dispatch_policy_reviewed_avx2_target_available`, gated `simd_dispatch_policy_avx2_selected`, and zero native handle, NUMA, GPU async-overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL side effects. AVX2 is isolated in target-local `mirakana_core_avx2` object code and selected only when compile/runtime gates pass. ARM NEON, broad Intel/AMD tuning, broad SIMD quality, GPU compute paths, cross-vendor/backend parity, and broad CPU/GPU/memory optimization remain follow-up work.
- Job Execution Placement Policy v1 adds host-independent `MK_core` placement evidence on top of completed topology and work-stealing decisions: `JobExecutionPlacementPolicyMode`, `JobExecutionPlacementPolicyStatus`, `JobExecutionPlacementPolicyDiagnosticCode`, `JobExecutionPlacementPolicyDesc`, `JobExecutionPlacementPolicy`, `select_job_execution_placement_policy`, and placement label helpers. The policy keeps OS scheduling as the default, preserves inherited worker count and `JobExecutionPoolDesc`, reports ready `os_default` rows, and fails closed to `host_evidence_required` for missing NUMA, hybrid-core, SMT, or manual host-affinity execution evidence. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-job-execution-placement-policy` reports `job_execution_placement_policy_status=ready`, `job_execution_placement_policy_ready=1`, `job_execution_placement_policy_requested_mode=os_default`, `job_execution_placement_policy_selected_mode=os_default`, `job_execution_placement_policy_host_evidence_required_diagnostics=1`, inherited two-worker work-stealing evidence, NUMA node count 1, zero performance/efficiency core counts, unknown SMT sibling topology, and zero affinity/NUMA/SIMD/GPU-overlap/CUDA/HIP/SYCL execution counters. Linux affinity execution, NUMA allocation execution, hybrid P-core/E-core pinning, SMT scheduling, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, CUDA/HIP/SYCL runtime paths, cross-vendor/backend parity, and broad all-core CPU/GPU/memory optimization claims remain follow-up work.
- Windows CPU Set Worker Placement v1 adds the narrow Windows host-owned execution lane over the placement policy foundation: `MK_core` exposes value-only worker-start placement requests/results and run counters, while `MK_platform_win32` exposes `Win32CpuSetRow`, `Win32CpuSetWorkerPlacementPlan`, `query_win32_cpu_sets`, `select_win32_cpu_set_worker_placement`, and `make_win32_cpu_set_worker_placement_callback` using official Windows CPU Sets APIs behind first-party rows. `sample_desktop_runtime_game --require-windows-cpu-set-worker-placement` reports package-visible ready status, two worker placement attempts/applies, a positive selected CPU Set count, two worker rows, zero diagnostics, `native_thread_handles_exposed=0`, and explicit zero Linux affinity / NUMA allocation / hybrid-SMT / SIMD / GPU async / CUDA / HIP / SYCL side-effect counters. Windows CPU Set SMT Worker Placement v1 is the active focused follow-up: `avoid_smt_siblings` selects distinct `CoreIndex` rows before SMT sibling CPU Sets, records `distinct_core_count`, `smt_sibling_cpu_set_count`, `smt_sibling_topology_known`, and `smt_sibling_policy_applied`, and the selected package smoke reports `windows_cpu_set_smt_worker_placement_status=ready`, positive `windows_cpu_set_smt_worker_placement_distinct_cores`, positive `windows_cpu_set_smt_worker_placement_smt_sibling_cpu_sets`, and `windows_cpu_set_smt_worker_placement_smt_policy_applied=1`. This is not hybrid P-core/E-core pinning, Linux affinity, NUMA memory allocation, broad SMT scheduling quality, broad SIMD quality, GPU async overlap, cross-vendor/backend parity, or broad CPU/GPU/memory optimization.
- Validation tooling includes strict clang-tidy compile database enforcement for the default Windows Visual Studio `dev` preset and the Linux `ci-linux-tidy` preset used by CI static analysis: `pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File tools/check-tidy.ps1` verifies `.clang-tidy`, requests/configures CMake File API codemodel data when native `compile_commands.json` is unavailable, synthesizes a clang-tidy-compatible compile database when needed, supports targeted changed-file analysis through `-Files`, and reports missing CMake or clang-tidy as local tool blockers.
- Production 1.0 Readiness Audit v1 adds `pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File tools/check-production-readiness-audit.ps1` as a default validation governance gate over `engine/agent/manifest.json.aiOperableProductionLoop.unsupportedProductionGaps`. After the Runtime Resource v2, Renderer RHI Resource Foundation, Frame Graph v1, Upload Staging v1, Scene/Prefab Schema v2 foundation, 2D playable vertical slice, 3D playable vertical slice, Editor Productization, Production UI Importer Platform Adapters, Full Repository Quality Gate, and 2026-05-19 gameplay/physics/navigation/AI closeouts, the composed manifest may report `production-readiness-audit: unsupported_gaps=0`. The audit still verifies every active unsupported row shape when rows exist, requires every `hostGates` row to publish a `residualClass`, prints `host_gate_residual_class[...]` counts, and keeps `ready` gates separate from `external-artifact-required`, `platform-host-required`, and `host-operation-required` residual work. `production-readiness-audit-check` remains the stable validation marker for this guard.
- CI Matrix Contract Check v1 adds `pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File tools/check-ci-matrix.ps1` as a default validation governance gate over `.github/workflows/validate.yml`, `.github/workflows/ios-validate.yml`, `engine/agent/manifest.json`, and `tools/validate.ps1`. It statically verifies the reviewed explicit Windows MSVC, Windows CPU profiling host, Windows asset importers, Windows native desktop editor, Windows ENet, Linux CMake, Linux Vulkan host, sanitizer, static-analysis, macOS Metal CMake, Metal host evidence, and iOS Metal jobs, `tools/classify-pr-validation-tier.ps1` docs-only/static-policy/runtime/workflow/optional-lane/non-PR classifier cases, SHA-pinned first-party GitHub Actions, `actions/checkout` least-privilege `persist-credentials: false` plus one transient fetch/auth retry, pinned Windows vcpkg checkout restoration, feature-scoped Windows vcpkg/build cache restore-save split, preset-backed Linux/macOS CMake lanes, Linux coverage artifacts, static-analysis tidy artifacts, test-log artifacts, guarded ccache stats after early checkout/toolchain failures, read-only workflow token permissions, stale same-ref PR/push/manual run cancellation, and host-gated iOS workflow evidence without executing CI locally or claiming signing, notarization, upload, release distribution, crash/telemetry backend readiness, or full optional host execution parity. Full Repository Static Analysis CI Contract v1 adds a `static-analysis` GitHub Actions lane that verifies the runner-provided Ubuntu toolchain, installs `ccache` only when missing, runs `tools/check-tidy.ps1 -Strict -Preset ci-linux-tidy -Jobs 0` with automatic CPU-count parallelism, and uploads `static-analysis-tidy-logs-<shard_index>`; broader static analyzer profile expansion remains future work outside the Engine 1.0 Windows-default ready claim.
- C++23 Release Package Artifact CI Evidence v1 extends the existing Windows C++23 release evaluation lane so release-only `tools/evaluate-cpp23.ps1 -Release` runs `Assert-ReleasePackageArtifacts` after CPack and the workflow uploads both the ZIP and `.zip.sha256` sidecar. The lane caches only the Release build/install trees it validates, avoids duplicate Debug C++23 work, uses automatic CMake/CTest parallelism, and has non-module tests/probes/samples/games opt out of CMake module dependency scanning while engine/library targets keep module scanning enabled. This still proves current package naming, checksum integrity, and required SDK archive entries without adding signing, upload, notarization, deployment, or full cross-platform package matrix readiness.
 - Installed SDK release validation now checks installed metadata before the clean consumer build: `tools/installed-sdk-validation.ps1` / `Assert-InstalledSdkMetadata` require CMake package config/version files, parseable installed AI manifest and schemas, non-empty installed workflow tools, the installed consumer example, at least one sample `game.agent.json`, docs README, third-party notices, the proprietary license payload, and absence of forbidden legacy desktop runtime DLLs in installed runtime artifacts. This does not add signing, upload, notarization, symbol-server, crash/telemetry backend, desktop-runtime selected-game smoke beyond the package lane, Android device matrix, or Apple-host readiness claims.
 - Desktop SDK release artifact validation now checks the current CPack ZIP and SHA-256 sidecar after package generation: `tools/release-package-artifacts.ps1` / `Assert-ReleasePackageArtifacts` derive the expected artifact basename from `CPackConfig.cmake`, compare the sidecar hash with the ZIP bytes, ignore stale unrelated ZIPs, reject forbidden legacy desktop runtime DLLs, and inspect required SDK metadata/tools/docs/notices/license entries without extracting or executing package contents. This does not add signing, upload, notarization, symbol-server, crash/telemetry backend, broad desktop-runtime selected-game package proof, Android device matrix, or Apple-host readiness claims.
- `MK_core` lifecycle, logging, deterministic diagnostics, counters, CPU profile capture, p95/p99 diagnostics budget summaries, memory diagnostics summaries, frame/worker scratch arena ownership, job scheduling diagnostics and bounded execution evidence summaries, Trace Event JSON export/review/reconstruction, and `DiagnosticsOpsPlan` operations handoff rows. `summarize_counter_budget` and `summarize_profile_budget` compute dependency-free nearest-rank `DiagnosticsBudgetSummary` rows over named `CounterSample` and `ProfileSample` data with count/min/average/p95/p99/max, missing-sample diagnostics, invalid non-finite counter diagnostics, invalid-threshold diagnostics, and threshold status before broader optimization claims. `ScratchArena`, `ScratchLease`, `ScratchLeaseStatus`, and `scratch_lease_status_label` provide bounded frame temporary and worker scratch buffers through non-owning `std::span<std::byte>` leases, non-copyable/non-movable arena owners, explicit `reset_at_safe_point` boundaries, owner checked worker releases, padding-aware capacity/high-water evidence, and `memory_counter_row` export. `summarize_memory_diagnostics` computes dependency-free `MemoryDiagnosticsSummary` rows over named `MemoryCounterRow` data with lifetime class aggregation, bytes/counts, reuse counts, reset counts, high-water bytes, budget pressure, invalid counter diagnostics, stale-generation diagnostics, use-after-safe-point diagnostics, cross-thread-free diagnostics, and false-sharing diagnostics. `summarize_job_scheduling_diagnostics` computes dependency-free `JobSchedulingDiagnosticsSummary` rows over `JobWorkerTopologyRow` and `JobQueueCounterRow` data with worker topology, processor-group/NUMA evidence, queue capacity/high-water, overflow, steal/wait, dependency, merge, scratch misuse, and job batch diagnostics. `build_job_scheduling_execution_evidence` turns `JobSchedulingWorkItemRow` inputs into deterministic `JobSchedulingExecutionOrderRow`, per-worker `JobQueueCounterRow`, per-worker scratch `MemoryCounterRow`, `JobSchedulingDiagnosticsSummary`, and `MemoryDiagnosticsSummary` evidence while detecting missing/blocked dependencies, cycles, queue overflow, cross-thread scratch misuse, nondeterministic merge attempts, and under/oversized batches without starting threads. `JobExecutionPool` provides real bounded `std::thread` worker execution with optional work stealing, and reports runtime steal attempt/success/wait counters through `JobExecutionRunResult` plus `JobSchedulingExecutionEvidence`. `build_diagnostics_ops_plan` reports ready summary/Chrome Trace Event JSON artifacts, host-gated crash dump review until the caller supplies Debugging Tools for Windows, symbols, dump policy, and operator handoff evidence, unsupported telemetry upload when no backend descriptor is supplied, and host-gated telemetry when the descriptor lacks OpenTelemetry `resourceSpans`/`service.name` contract review, local path redaction, secret redaction, or operator handoff evidence. `DiagnosticsTraceImportReview` / `review_diagnostics_trace_json` provide dependency-free structured review of the supported Trace Event JSON subset, and `DiagnosticsTraceImportResult` / `import_diagnostics_trace_json` reconstruct only first-party exported `M`/`i`/`C`/`X` rows into `DiagnosticCapture` data. Native dump writing, crash-report backends, telemetry SDKs/uploads, symbol publication, OS handles, network dependencies, arbitrary JSON conversion beyond that first-party subset, native thread handles, affinity masks, NUMA placement controls, global allocator hooks/enforcement, broad pool policy, and flame graphs remain unsupported.

  - Runtime Texture Upload Multi-Queue Final-State Evidence v1: byte-backed `upload_runtime_texture` now builds a one-pass imported-texture schedule, records the copy command through `execute_frame_graph_rhi_multi_queue_schedule`, prepares `copy_destination` through `FrameGraphTexturePassTargetState`, restores `shader_read` through `FrameGraphTextureFinalState`, and reports command-list, queue-wait, total barrier, pass-target, final-state, and callback counters on `RuntimeTextureUploadResult`. Runtime Mesh Frame Graph Command Evidence v1, Runtime Skinned Mesh Frame Graph Command Evidence v1, Runtime Morph Mesh Frame Graph Command Evidence v1, and Runtime Material Factor Frame Graph Command Evidence v1 add one-pass command-list ownership evidence for byte-backed `upload_runtime_mesh`, `upload_runtime_skinned_mesh`, `upload_runtime_morph_mesh_cpu`, and material-factor uniform copies. Metadata-only texture allocations still report zero Frame Graph evidence, and buffer barriers, broad/background streaming, runtime-wide ring ownership beyond reviewed texture/buffer uploads, production graph ownership, async overlap, and public native/RHI handles remain unsupported.
  - RHI Native Async Upload Execution v1: `execute_upload_gpu_batch_async` submits a caller-owned `RhiUploadStagingPlan` / `RhiUploadRing` batch on a selected backend-neutral queue, returns `RhiUploadGpuBatchExecutionResult` with the submitted `FenceValue`, and performs no helper-owned CPU wait after prevalidating target counts and ring ownership. Runtime Upload Queue Wait v1 adds `wait_for_runtime_uploads_on_queue`, `RuntimeUploadQueueWaitResult`, and package mesh/skinned/morph `upload_queue_waits_recorded` result fields so package transactions with async copy-queue uploads can record graphics-queue waits for returned upload fences without CPU waits or native handle exposure. Staging Pool Lease Adoption v1 adds `RhiStagingBufferLease`, `RhiStagingBufferPool::try_acquire_lease`, `RhiStagingBufferPool::release(RhiStagingBufferLease)`, and `RhiUploadRingDesc::buffer` so a host-owned pool chunk can back a caller-owned upload ring without allocating another ring buffer. Runtime-wide staging-pool ownership beyond explicit leases, allocator/GPU budgets, public native handles, and async overlap/performance remain unsupported.
  - Frame Graph Automatic Aliasing Barrier Insertion v1: `execute_frame_graph_rhi_texture_schedule` can take `FrameGraphTransientTextureLifetime` rows and automatically record one backend-neutral `IRhiCommandList::texture_aliasing_barrier` before the first pass that uses each later resource in a non-overlapping transient alias group, reporting `aliasing_barriers_recorded`. Invalid lifetime ranges, missing bindings, duplicate lifetime rows, overlapping alias lifetimes, or same-handle automatic aliases fail before command recording or pass callbacks. Frame Graph Transient Alias Content Initialization v1 rejects resource-backed transient first render-pass `LoadAction::load` rows before aliasing barriers, render pass begin/end, or pass callbacks. Frame Graph Multi-Queue Automatic Aliasing Barrier Execution v1 extends `execute_frame_graph_rhi_multi_queue_schedule` with `FrameGraphRhiMultiQueueExecutionDesc::transient_texture_lifetimes` and `FrameGraphRhiMultiQueueExecutionResult::aliasing_barriers_recorded`; aliasing barriers record after producer waits and before scheduled texture barriers, target states, render-pass envelopes, or callbacks, and the same first render-pass load rejection happens before command-list creation. Frame Graph RHI Multi-Queue Texture Barrier Execution v1 lets `execute_frame_graph_rhi_multi_queue_schedule` take optional `FrameGraphRhiMultiQueueExecutionDesc::texture_bindings` rows and report `FrameGraphRhiMultiQueueExecutionResult::barriers_recorded`; supplied bindings make scheduled texture barriers validate before command recording and record on the consumer pass command list after producer waits and before callbacks. Frame Graph Multi-Queue Render Pass Execution v1 extends that multi-queue executor with optional `pass_target_accesses`, `pass_target_states`, and `render_passes` rows, records target-state transitions after waits/barriers and before graphics callbacks, begins/ends render-pass envelopes around graphics callbacks, reports `pass_target_state_barriers_recorded` and `render_passes_recorded`, and rejects swapchain or non-graphics render-pass rows before command-list creation. Frame Graph Backend-Neutral Distinct Alias-Group Lease Binding v1 still binds validated transient texture alias groups to one backend-neutral alias-group lease with distinct `TextureHandle` rows per resource. Frame Graph Shared Texture State Handoff v1 remains for caller-provided shared-handle rows, and Frame Graph Texture Aliasing Barrier Command v1 records explicit resource-name alias dependencies without changing tracked texture states, and Public Null Aliasing Barriers v1 treats `TextureHandle{}` plus empty Frame Graph aliasing resource names as backend-neutral wildcard endpoints. D3D12 one-texture leases still prove one-private-heap placed allocation, first-use activation barriers, and deferred placed-resource retirement; multi-texture alias-group leases use backend-private same-offset placed resources and can feed automatic or explicit non-null aliasing barrier/state evidence. Vulkan alias-group leases now use distinct alias-flagged images over one shared backend-private `VkDeviceMemory` allocation and first-party transient texture counters. Metal alias memory execution, actual data inheritance/content preservation, production multi-queue graph adoption, async overlap/performance evidence, package streaming integration, and broad renderer quality remain unsupported.

headless source-tree game object; `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` now reports package-visible `gameplay_systems_perception_readiness_status=ready`,
