- Physics Collision Query v1 adds value-only `PhysicsCollisionQueryBatchStatus`, `PhysicsCollisionQueryBatchDiagnostic`, `PhysicsCollisionQueryRowStatus`, `PhysicsCollisionQueryRowDiagnostic`, `PhysicsRaycastBatch2DDesc`, `PhysicsRaycastBatch3DDesc`, `PhysicsShapeSweepBatch2DDesc`, and `PhysicsShapeSweepBatch3DDesc` rows plus `PhysicsWorld2D::raycast_batch`, `PhysicsWorld3D::raycast_batch`, `PhysicsWorld2D::shape_sweep_batch`, and `PhysicsWorld3D::shape_sweep_batch`. Batches preserve source order, return per-query hit/no-hit/invalid-request diagnostics, use default-unbounded query counts unless a positive `max_queries` budget is set, and reuse existing ray mask, collision layer/mask, ignored-body, trigger-inclusion, and nearest-hit behavior without exposing native physics handles. `PhysicsCollisionQuery3DReadinessConfig`, `PhysicsCollisionQuery3DReadinessReport`, and `evaluate_physics_collision_query_readiness_3d` summarize selected 3D raycast/sweep batch evidence for raycast hits, shape-sweep hits, no-hit rows, invalid-request rows, budget rejections, source ordering, row budgets, and diagnostics.

## Ready AI-Operable Surfaces

These reviewed surfaces are ready within their documented scopes:

- `register-runtime-package-files`: reviewed `runtimePackageFiles` appends through the existing tool/editor-core lanes.
- `register-source-asset`: `GameEngine.SourceAssetRegistry.v1` rows plus deterministic Asset Identity and import-metadata projections. It does not execute importers, write cooked artifacts, update `.geindex`, or create renderer/RHI resources.
- `cook-registered-source-assets`: `GameEngine.SourceAssetRegistry.v1` 行を、明示的に選択したキー集合、または `dependencyExpansion=registered_source_registry_closure` かつ `dependencyCooking=registry_closure` のとき **同一レジストリ文書内の依存キー閉包**まで含めて、決定的な調理成果物とランタイム読み込み可能な `.geindex` に変換する（`plan_registered_source_asset_cook_package` / `apply_registered_source_asset_cook_package`）。既定は明示選択。外部 Importer、レジストリ外の推論、レンダラ／RHI 常駐、パッケージストリーミング、グラフオーサリング、ライブシェーダ生成、エディタ製品化、Metal、公開ネイティブハンドル、任意シェル、自由形式編集は対象外のまま。
- Registered Source Asset Cook Targets（`game.agent.json.registeredSourceAssetCookTargets`）: 3D デスクトップパッケージ等で、`cook-registered-source-assets` に渡す **レビュー済みのルートキー**、`dependencyExpansion` / `dependencyCooking`、および対応する `prefabScenePackageAuthoringTargets` 行との整合（同一 `sourceRegistryPath` / `packageIndexPath`）をマニフェスト上で固定するデスクリプタのみ。コマンド文字列やシェル実行は含まない。
- `create-material-from-graph`: reviewed `GameEngine.MaterialGraph.v1` graph text or selected graph file -> runtime `GameEngine.Material.v1` `.material` package update through `mirakana::plan_material_graph_package_update` / `mirakana::apply_material_graph_package_update`. It validates package-relative paths, source revision, existing texture rows, `AssetKind::material` output rows, and deterministic `material_texture` edges without shader graph generation, live shader generation, shader compiler execution, renderer/RHI residency, package streaming, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, or broad renderer quality claims.
- `create-scene`, `add-scene-node`, `add-or-update-component`, `create-prefab`, `instantiate-prefab`, and `refresh-prefab-instance`: reviewed `GameEngine.Scene.v2` / `GameEngine.Prefab.v2` authoring commands.
- `migrate-scene-v2-runtime-package`: reviewed bridge from authored `GameEngine.Scene.v2` plus `GameEngine.SourceAssetRegistry.v1` rows into the existing `GameEngine.Scene.v1` `.scene` plus `.geindex` package update surface.
- Validated authored-to-runtime workflow: `register-source-asset -> cook-registered-source-assets -> migrate-scene-v2-runtime-package -> validate-runtime-scene-package`. This host-independent workflow proof executes the package load and `MK_runtime_scene` instantiation through the validation helper; it is not a new broad orchestration command.
- `validate-runtime-scene-package`: non-mutating runtime scene package validation through `mirakana::plan_runtime_scene_package_validation` and `mirakana::execute_runtime_scene_package_validation` for explicit `.geindex` package load plus `MK_runtime_scene` instantiation diagnostics. Optional `contentRoot` is a prefix applied to package entry paths; omit it when `.geindex` entries already include the runtime-relative directory. It does not cook packages, parse source assets at runtime, create renderer/RHI residency, stream packages, productize editor flows, expose native handles, or support arbitrary shell/free-form edits.
- `game.agent.json.runtimeSceneValidationTargets`: descriptor-only rows for selecting reviewed `validate-runtime-scene-package` inputs from game manifests. Rows carry a safe game-relative `.geindex` path, an explicit scene asset key, optional content root, and validation flags; contentRoot must not duplicate prefixes already present in cooked package entry paths. Rows are not command strings, package mutation, runtime source parsing, renderer/RHI residency, package streaming, editor productization, native handles, or renderer quality claims.
- Editor Playtest Package Review Loop v1: an ordered review/run contract over existing editor package candidates, reviewed `runtimePackageFiles` registration, manifest-declared `runtimeSceneValidationTargets`, `validate-runtime-scene-package`, and host-gated desktop smoke recipes. It sequences existing surfaces; it is not play-in-editor isolation, broad package cooking, renderer/RHI residency, package streaming, native handle exposure, Metal readiness, or full editor productization.
- Editor Runtime Scene Package Validation Execution v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorRuntimeScenePackageValidationExecutionDesc`, `EditorRuntimeScenePackageValidationExecutionModel`, `EditorRuntimeScenePackageValidationExecutionResult`, `make_editor_runtime_scene_package_validation_execution_model`, `execute_editor_runtime_scene_package_validation`, and `make_editor_runtime_scene_package_validation_execution_ui_model` execute the existing non-mutating package validation command from reviewed `EditorPlaytestPackageReviewModel` rows and retain package record, scene node, reference, blocker, and diagnostic evidence. The visible AI Commands panel exposes `Validate Runtime Scene Package` through `mirakana::RootedFileSystem` state. It does not cook packages, parse source assets, run external processes, execute arbitrary shell or validation recipes, mutate manifests, productize Play-In-Editor, load dynamic game modules, create renderer/RHI residency, stream packages, expose native handles, make Metal ready, or claim broad renderer quality.
- Play-In-Editor Session Isolation v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorPlaySession` snapshots a `SceneAuthoringDocument` source scene into an isolated simulation scene copy, reports source-scene edit blocking while active, tracks simulation ticks in play state, supports begin/pause/resume/tick/stop transitions, and discards simulation edits on stop. It is an editor-core isolation contract only; it does not execute game code, physics/audio ticks, package scripts, renderer/RHI uploads, hot reload, package streaming, native handles, or full editor productization.
- Play-In-Editor Gameplay Driver v1: `mirakana::editor::IEditorPlaySessionDriver` lets a caller attach reviewed begin/tick/end callbacks to an `EditorPlaySession`; callbacks receive only the isolated simulation scene plus `EditorPlaySessionTickContext` frame/delta rows. It validates finite positive tick deltas, rejects ticks while paused, records the last delta, and calls `on_play_end` before discarding the simulation scene. It does not load dynamic game modules, embed `DesktopGameRunner`, execute package scripts or validation recipes, create renderer/RHI uploads, expose native handles, run hot reload, or stream packages.
- Play-In-Editor Visible Viewport Wiring v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorPlaySessionControlsModel` exposes deterministic Play/Pause/Resume/Stop command rows and `viewport_uses_simulation_scene`; the future visible `MK_editor` Run menu and Viewport toolbar now drive `EditorPlaySession`, render the isolated simulation scene while active, tick once per viewport frame in play state, and reject source-scene authoring plus undo/redo while source edits are blocked. It does not add dynamic game module loading, runtime host embedding, package scripts, validation recipe execution, renderer/RHI uploads from editor core, native handles, hot reload, package streaming, or a full Unity/UE-like workflow.
- Editor Viewport Vulkan RHI Bootstrap v1 (Windows `MK_editor` when built with `MK_ENABLE_DESKTOP_EDITOR`): links `MK_rhi_vulkan`, exposes optional headless `VulkanRuntimeDevice` bridged to `IRhiDevice` via `mirakana::rhi::vulkan::minimal_irhi_device_mapping_plan` when the Vulkan loader probe and viewport SPIR-V artifact readiness gates pass, and selects SPIR-V viewport plus material-preview shader bytecode when the active render backend is Vulkan; The old desktop editor texture display interop path has been removed; future visible editor viewport display must use a first-party platform/rendering adapter. Default repository `dev` configure keeps `MK_ENABLE_DESKTOP_EDITOR=OFF`, so `MK_editor` is optional at configure time.
- Editor Runtime Host Playtest Launch v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorRuntimeHostPlaytestLaunchDesc`, `EditorRuntimeHostPlaytestLaunchModel`, `make_editor_runtime_host_playtest_launch_model`, and `make_editor_runtime_host_playtest_launch_ui_model` review caller-supplied desktop runtime-host argv, working directory, host gates, acknowledgements, and unsupported claims before exposing a safe `mirakana::ProcessCommand` plus retained `play_in_editor.runtime_host` rows. The future visible `MK_editor` Run/Viewport UI can acknowledge the `d3d12-windows-primary` host gate, execute the reviewed external runtime-host command through `mirakana::Win32ProcessRunner` on Windows, and store transient exit/stdout/stderr evidence. It does not add dynamic game-module loading, in-process runtime-host embedding, package scripts, arbitrary shell, raw manifest command evaluation, free-form manifest edits, renderer/RHI/native handles, hot reload, package streaming, or full editor productization.
- Editor In-Process Runtime Host Review v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorInProcessRuntimeHostDesc`, `EditorInProcessRuntimeHostModel`, `EditorInProcessRuntimeHostBeginResult`, `make_editor_in_process_runtime_host_model`, `begin_editor_in_process_runtime_host_session`, and `make_editor_in_process_runtime_host_ui_model` review an already-linked `IEditorPlaySessionDriver` before starting the existing isolated `EditorPlaySession` and exposing retained `play_in_editor.in_process_runtime_host` rows.
- Editor Dynamic Game Module Driver Load v1, Editor Game Module Driver Safe Reload Review v1, Editor Game Module Driver Contract Metadata Review v1, Editor Game Module Driver Dynamic Probe v1, Editor Game Module Driver CTest Probe Evidence UI v1, Editor Game Module Driver Reload Transaction Recipe MK Editor Evidence v1, and Editor Game Module Driver Play Session Gate Review v1: `mirakana::DynamicLibrary`, `mirakana::load_dynamic_library`, `mirakana::resolve_dynamic_library_symbol`, `mirakana::editor::EditorGameModuleDriverApi`, `EditorGameModuleDriverContractMetadataModel`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_reload_model`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_reload_ui_model`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_ctest_probe_evidence_model`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_ctest_probe_evidence_ui_model`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_reload_transaction_recipe_evidence_model`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_reload_transaction_recipe_evidence_ui_model`, `editor_game_module_driver_reload_transaction_recipe_evidence_contract_v1`, `make_editor_game_module_driver_unload_model`, `can_load` / `can_unload`. The Viewport panel exposes `Game Module Driver`, `Load Game Module Driver`, `Reload Game Module Driver`, and `Unload Game Module Driver`, resolves `mirakana_create_editor_game_module_driver_v1`, keeps retained `play_in_editor.game_module_driver`, `play_in_editor.game_module_driver.reload`, `play_in_editor.game_module_driver.contract`, `play_in_editor.game_module_driver.ctest_probe_evidence`, `play_in_editor.game_module_driver.reload_transaction_recipe_evidence`, and `play_in_editor.game_module_driver.unload` rows, and enables `Begin In-Process Runtime Host` only while a driver is loaded. It does not add active-session hot reload, stable third-party binary ABI, `DesktopGameRunner` embedding, package scripts, validation recipe execution, arbitrary shell, renderer/RHI uploads or handles, package streaming, native handles, or full editor productization. **Engine 1.0 policy:** vendor-stable third-party C ABI for out-of-tree editor DLLs is explicitly out of scope; see `docs/legal-and-licensing.md` and `Editor Game Module Driver Stable Third Party ABI 1 0 Exclusion v1`.
- Editor Scene Native Dialog v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorSceneFileDialogModel`, `make_scene_open_dialog_request`, `make_scene_save_dialog_request`, `make_scene_open_dialog_model`, `make_scene_save_dialog_model`, and `make_scene_file_dialog_ui_model` build and review native `.scene` open/save dialog requests/results under retained `scene_file_dialog.open` / `scene_file_dialog.save` rows without putting SDL3, Dear ImGui, native handles, filesystem IO, or project-store path conversion in editor core. The future visible `MK_editor` File menu and Scene panel expose `Open Scene...`, `Save Scene As...`, `Browse Open Scene`, and `Browse Save Scene As` through `native shell file-dialog service`; accepted in-project `.scene` selections are converted to safe project-relative paths, save-as updates `SceneAuthoringDocument::set_scene_path`, and scene replacement reuses the path that stops active Play-In-Editor and clears undo state.
- Editor Project Native Dialog v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorProjectFileDialogModel`, `EditorProjectFileDialogMode`, `make_project_open_dialog_request`, `make_project_save_dialog_request`, `make_project_open_dialog_model`, `make_project_save_dialog_model`, and `make_project_file_dialog_ui_model` build and review native `.geproject` open/save dialog requests/results under retained `project_file_dialog.open` / `project_file_dialog.save` rows without putting SDL3, Dear ImGui, native handles, filesystem IO, or project-store path conversion in editor core. The future visible `MK_editor` File menu and Project Settings panel expose `Open Project...` and `Save Project As...` through `native shell file-dialog service`; accepted in-store `.geproject` selections are converted to safe store-relative paths before reusing `load_project_bundle` / `save_project_bundle` and the existing scene replacement path.
- Editor Resource Panel Diagnostics v1, Resource Capture Request v1, and Resource Capture Execution Evidence v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorResourcePanelModel` and `make_editor_resource_panel_model` expose deterministic read-only status, counter, memory, lifetime, reviewed capture request, and host-owned capture execution evidence rows from caller-supplied plain resource diagnostics; retained `MK_ui` output includes `resources.capture_requests` labels for action, host gates, acknowledgement, and diagnostics plus `resources.capture_execution` labels for evidence `phase_code`, status, host gates, bounded artifact paths, bounded diagnostic rows, the stable contract root `ge.editor.resources_capture_execution.v1` on `resources.capture_execution.contract_label`, and `ge.editor.resources_capture_operator_validated_launch_workflow.v1` on `resources.capture_execution.operator_validated_launch_workflow_contract_label` through `EditorResourceCaptureExecutionInput` / `EditorResourceCaptureExecutionRow`. The native `MK_editor` Resources panel now renders this model and refreshes it from live D3D12 host availability before panel rendering; fuller active viewport RHI `stats()`, `memory_diagnostics()`, optional lifetime registry, D3D12-only PIX/debug-layer request acknowledgement, and waiting evidence remain service/viewport follow-up work. It does not launch PIX automatically, toggle D3D12 debug-layer APIs, run ETW/performance capture, enforce residency, implement allocator policy, evict resources, stream packages, execute arbitrary GPU captures from editor core, migrate backend destruction, expose native handles, or make a general renderer quality claim. Optional Windows operator helper `tools/launch-pix-host-helper.ps1` (plan `Editor Resource Capture PIX Launch Helper v1`) supports host-side PIX launch from a non-repository scratch directory after reviewing capture rows; see also `Editor Resource Capture PIX Host Handoff Evidence v1` and `Editor Resources Capture Operator Validated Launch Workflow v1`.
- Editor Content Browser Import Diagnostics v1, Native Dialog v1, External Copy Review v1, External Copy Transaction v1, and Codec Adapter Review v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorContentBrowserImportPanelModel`, `make_editor_content_browser_import_panel_model`, and `make_content_browser_import_panel_ui_model` expose the visible Assets panel as a deterministic read-only model over `ContentBrowserState`, `AssetPipelineState`, import progress, diagnostics, dependencies, thumbnail requests, selected material preview rows, and hot-reload summaries. Persistent Provenance Gate v1 adds `mirakana::AssetImportProvenanceDocumentV1`, `AssetImportProvenanceRowV1`, `serialize_asset_import_provenance_document`, `deserialize_asset_import_provenance_document`, `validate_asset_import_provenance_document`, and `mirakana::editor::make_editor_asset_browser_legal_provenance_row` records/projection for asset-key, origin, source, license, notice, and external-engine-material gates. `mirakana::editor::EditorContentBrowserImportOpenDialogModel`, `make_content_browser_import_open_dialog_request`, `make_content_browser_import_open_dialog_model`, and `make_content_browser_import_open_dialog_ui_model` add reviewed multi-select import source selection under retained `content_browser_import.open_dialog` rows. `mirakana::editor::EditorContentBrowserImportExternalSourceCopyModel`, `make_content_browser_import_external_source_copy_model`, and `make_content_browser_import_external_source_copy_ui_model` add reviewed external source copy staging under retained `content_browser_import.external_copy` rows; the visible `MK_editor` shell now adds native Source Pulse handoff by routing `Browse Import Sources` through `native shell file-dialog service`, canonicalizing accepted in-project `.texture`, `.mesh`, `.material`, `.scene`, `.audio_source`, `.png`, `.gltf`, `.glb`, `.wav`, `.mp3`, and `.flac` selections to safe project-relative paths, rejecting selections outside the project root or with invalid/device paths, using explicit `Copy External Sources` review to stage external reviewed sources only under `ProjectDocument::asset_root/imported_sources/<filename>`, executing `NativeEditorApp::copy_reviewed_asset_browser_external_sources` / `asset_browser.import.copy_external_sources` only after matching-generation user confirmation and legal provenance review, copying through shell-private `.copying-*` temp targets while rejecting device paths, traversal, symlinks, non-regular sources, and collisions, and applying copied project-relative source registrations through `NativeEditorApp::apply_reviewed_asset_browser_import_sources` / `asset_browser.import.register_sources` before refreshing Source Pulse import planning. Explicit `Import Assets` reaches `execute_asset_import_plan` with `mirakana::ExternalAssetImportAdapters::options()` only after the `asset_browser.import.execute_reviewed_plan` row passes matching-generation and user-confirmation review through the native shell asset-import filesystem service; successful batches register imported asset records, refresh Source Pulse import status from `AssetPipelineState`, refresh browser rows from the active source registry, and increment generation, while failed batches write no partial cooked outputs, register no visible asset records, and keep the browser generation unchanged. This does not add arbitrary file import, arbitrary importer adapters, automatic import execution, arbitrary shell, package scripts, validation execution, free-form manifest edits, package streaming, renderer/RHI/native handles, legal advice, external-engine project/schema/asset/UI compatibility, or broad editor/importer readiness.
- Folder And Drag-Drop Batch Review v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorContentBrowserImportFolderScanModel`, `EditorContentBrowserImportFolderScanRequest`, `make_content_browser_import_folder_scan_model`, `make_content_browser_import_folder_scan_ui_model`, and `make_content_browser_import_drag_drop_model` add value-only batch source review. Folder scans feed existing `EditorAssetImportCandidateInput` rows while enforcing maximum 500 candidates, 4 directory levels, and 256 MiB per file unless a reviewed override is supplied. `NativeEditorApp::review_asset_browser_folder_import_scan` lists through shell-owned `IFileSystem`, and `NativeEditorApp::review_asset_browser_drag_drop_import_sources` normalizes project drops to the same retained `content_browser_import.open_dialog` ids while routing external absolute file drops to the existing external-copy review. These review paths do not copy, register, import, start jobs, expose OS drag/drop handles, execute tools, add dependencies, provide legal advice, or claim Unity/Unreal/Godot compatibility.
- Import Job Queue And Progress v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorAssetImportJobSnapshot`, `EditorAssetImportJobRow`, `EditorAssetImportJobCommandKind`, `make_editor_asset_import_job_model`, `plan_editor_asset_import_job_command`, and `apply_editor_asset_import_job_command` add deterministic value-only Source Pulse job rows for reviewed copy/import batches. The native `MK_editor` shell now starts one job after the existing legal/provenance, generation, user-confirmation, and filesystem gates pass, returns job ids from reviewed external-copy and import execution results, records `queued`, `copying`, `registering`, `importing`, `refreshing`, `succeeded`, `failed`, and `canceled` states, and applies generation-checked cooperative cancel/retry. Retry appends a new queued child job without mutating the completed failed/canceled row; cancel applies before the next mutation boundary. Job rows expose no native handles and do not add automatic import execution, background workers, package scripts, validation execution, renderer/RHI residency, external-engine compatibility, legal advice, or new third-party dependencies.
- Reviewed Reimport Recook And Hot Reload v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorAssetReimportReviewRequest`, `EditorAssetRecookReviewRequest`, `EditorAssetHotReloadStageReviewRequest`, `EditorAssetImportReviewedActionPlan`, `review_editor_asset_reimport_request`, `review_editor_asset_recook_request`, and `review_editor_asset_hot_reload_stage_request` add value-only reviewed rows for `asset_browser.import.reimport_selected`, `asset_browser.import.recook_stale`, and `asset_browser.import.stage_hot_reload`. Reimport is selected by `AssetKeyV2`, dependency closure is opt-in, stale recook rows require caller-supplied source/output content hashes and reuse `build_asset_recook_plan`, and hot reload review separates staged replacements from caller-owned safe-point commits while reporting `parses_runtime_sources=false`. The native `MK_editor` shell adds `execute_reviewed_asset_browser_reimport_selection`, `execute_reviewed_asset_browser_recook`, and `commit_staged_asset_browser_hot_reload`; recook execution goes through existing `execute_asset_runtime_recook` after matching-generation user confirmation, stages replacements in `AssetRuntimeReplacementState`, records failed recook rollback rows, and commits only at the explicit safe point. This does not add automatic file watching, runtime source parsing, active-session game-module hot reload, package streaming, renderer/RHI residency, public native handles, external-engine compatibility, legal advice, or new third-party dependencies.
- Asset Import Presets v1: `mirakana::AssetImportPresetsDocumentV1`, `AssetImportTexturePresetV1`, `AssetImportMeshPresetV1`, `AssetImportAudioPresetV1`, `serialize_asset_import_presets_document`, `deserialize_asset_import_presets_document`, `validate_asset_import_presets_document`, `is_valid_asset_import_mesh_preset_v1`, and `review_asset_import_preset_for_asset` add locale-independent deterministic `GameEngine.AssetImportPresets.v1` project defaults and per-`AssetKeyV2` overrides for texture, mesh, and audio import intent. `review_editor_asset_import_candidates` copies reviewed preset metadata plus the effective `AssetImportMeshPresetV1` into candidate rows and `AssetImportAction::mesh_preset`; unsupported combinations such as tangent generation without normals or streaming source review with peak normalization block the matching import row with `asset_import_preset_unsupported` instead of being ignored or leaking to unrelated rows. `MK_tools` consumes mesh `unit_scale` / `up_axis` for selected glTF mesh, morph mesh CPU, and node transform animation import paths, baking supported data into the project right-handed +Y-up meter convention. Texture/audio presets and unsupported transform paths remain value-only or fail closed, and presets do not add codec execution by themselves, parser type exposure, runtime source parsing, external-engine compatibility, legal advice, or new dependencies.
- Editor Content Browser Asset Identity v2 Rows v1, Source Registry Population v1, Editor Source Registry Visible Content Browser v1, and Source Pulse Production Rows v1: `ContentBrowserState::refresh_from(const AssetRegistry&, const AssetIdentityDocumentV2&)` read-only annotates existing cooked registry rows with `AssetKeyV2` labels and source paths derived by `asset_id_from_key_v2`; `ContentBrowserState::refresh_from(const SourceAssetRegistryDocumentV1&)` builds deterministic rows directly from `GameEngine.SourceAssetRegistry.v1` entries using derived `AssetId`, `imported_path`, stable key labels, source paths, and `identity_backed=true`; `ContentBrowserState::select(const AssetKeyV2&)` selects the derived id. The visible `MK_editor` Assets panel reads first-party Source Pulse `asset_browser.*` rows from project source-registry value data, reads the active `GameEngine.Project.v4` `project.source_registry` path through `refresh_content_browser_from_project_source_registry`, reports source registry path/status/asset count, selected `Asset Key` / source labels, and explicit reviewed command plans including `Reload Source Registry` and confirmation-gated import execution. `EditorAssetBrowserProductionModel`, `make_editor_asset_browser_production_model`, and `make_editor_asset_browser_production_ui_model` expose deterministic retained `asset_browser.status`, `asset_browser.query`, `asset_browser.source_registry.path`, per-source key/path/state/package-status rows, `asset_browser.commands.*`, `asset_browser.legal.*`, `asset_browser.preview.*`, and `asset_browser.package.*` rows. `EditorAssetBrowserPreviewEvidenceRow`, `EditorAssetBrowserPreviewEvidenceDesc`, and `make_editor_asset_browser_preview_evidence_rows` aggregate host-owned material preview snapshots, thumbnail requests, glTF mesh primitive inspect reports, audio metadata summaries, scene-reference diagnostics, and hot-reload recook requests; the native shell refreshes these rows from private material-preview evidence and import-plan thumbnail requests without exposing native handles. `EditorAssetBrowserPackageReviewDesc` and `make_editor_asset_browser_package_review_model` adapt existing scene package candidate/draft/apply contracts into package review rows that classify add, already-registered, source-only, unsafe, duplicate, missing-cooked-artifact, and blocked-license candidates, with mutation narrowed to reviewed `game.agent.json.runtimePackageFiles` edits through `apply_scene_package_registration_to_manifest` and `ITextStore`. This closes visible editor asset browser migration for project-owned source registry rows, shell-owned reviewed import/preview evidence, retained UI/legal/command rows, and value-only package review rows; arbitrary importer adapters, automatic import execution, package script execution, validation recipe execution, broad runtime package streaming, renderer/RHI residency from editor core, public native handles, Vulkan/Metal preview display parity, cross-platform accessibility parity, external-engine compatibility/equivalence/parity, and Unity/Unreal/Godot asset/project/schema import compatibility remain unsupported.
- Editor Material Asset Preview Diagnostics v1 and GPU Preview Execution Evidence v1: `mirakana::editor::EditorMaterialAssetPreviewPanelModel`, `EditorMaterialGpuPreviewExecutionSnapshot`, `make_editor_material_asset_preview_panel_model`, `apply_editor_material_gpu_preview_execution_snapshot`, and `make_material_asset_preview_panel_ui_model` expose selected cooked material metadata, factor rows, texture dependency diagnostics, typed GPU payload texture rows, D3D12/Vulkan material-preview shader readiness rows, and retained `material_asset_preview.gpu.execution` evidence rows for the Assets panel. The optional `MK_editor` shell remains the only place that uploads runtime textures, creates material descriptor bindings, renders the small `RhiViewportSurface`, and displays the future editor viewport texture; viewport color-state transitions are executor-owned inside `MK_renderer`, while shader compiler execution, package scripts, package streaming, native handles, Vulkan swapchain-backed viewport Dear ImGui texture display parity, Metal readiness, and broad editor/renderer readiness remain outside editor core.
- Editor Productization is closed for the Engine 1.0 Windows-default ready surface through reviewed editor authoring/playtest/AI command/resource/input/prefab/material-preview evidence. Vulkan/Metal material-preview display parity, broad Unity/UE-like editor parity, active-session hot reload execution, automatic fuzzy nested prefab merge/rebase UX, automatic capture/ETW/debug-layer execution, stable third-party editor DLL ABI, and unacknowledged host-gated AI command execution are explicit future or host-gated exclusions rather than remaining Windows-default blockers.
- Editor Prefab Variant Conflict Review v1, Reviewed Resolution v1, Missing Node Cleanup v1, Node Retarget Review v1, Source Mismatch Retarget Review v1, Source Mismatch Accept Current Review v1, Batch Resolution Review v1, Native Dialog v1, and Base Refresh Merge Review v1: `mirakana::editor::PrefabVariantConflictReviewModel`, `PrefabVariantConflictRow`, `PrefabVariantConflictBatchResolutionPlan`, `make_prefab_variant_conflict_review_model`, `make_prefab_variant_conflict_review_ui_model`, `resolve_prefab_variant_conflict`, `resolve_prefab_variant_conflicts`, `make_prefab_variant_conflict_resolution_action`, `make_prefab_variant_conflict_batch_resolution_action`, and `mirakana::deserialize_prefab_variant_definition_for_review` expose prefab variant override review rows with stable `prefab_variant_conflicts` and `prefab_variant_conflicts.batch_resolution` retained `MK_ui` ids and future visible `MK_editor` Conflict Review rows. `PrefabNodeOverride::source_node_name` is an optional first-party hint serialized as `override.N.source_node_name`; editor-created name/transform/component overrides populate it from the current base prefab node. The model reports blocking missing-node, duplicate-override, and `source_node_mismatch` rows, non-blocking redundant/component-family warnings, whether the variant can compose, explicit cleanup actions for redundant/later duplicate/stale missing-node overrides, explicit retarget actions when a stale missing-node override has a non-empty source-node hint that uniquely matches one current base node without creating a duplicate node/kind override, explicit retarget actions when an existing-node `source_node_mismatch` row uniquely matches a different current base node, explicit `Accept current node N` / `accept_current_node` hint repair that updates only `source_node_name` when no safe unique retarget exists, and one undoable reviewed `Apply All Reviewed` batch path. `EditorPrefabVariantFileDialogModel`, `make_prefab_variant_open_dialog_request`, `make_prefab_variant_save_dialog_request`, `make_prefab_variant_open_dialog_model`, `make_prefab_variant_save_dialog_model`, and `make_prefab_variant_file_dialog_ui_model` add the first non-Profiler native document dialog slice with retained `prefab_variant_file_dialog.open` / `prefab_variant_file_dialog.save` rows for accepted/canceled/failed `.prefabvariant` open/save selections; the visible shell exposes `Browse Load Variant` and `Browse Save Variant` through `native shell file-dialog service` and converts accepted in-project selections to safe project-relative paths before reusing existing load/save helpers. Cleanup, retarget, accept-current, batch apply, and dialog selection handling are never automatic, go through reviewed `UndoStack` or existing `.prefabvariant` IO paths in the visible editor, and do not mutate files, scenes, manifests, packages, or runtime state from the editor-core models. `PrefabVariantBaseRefreshPlan`, `PrefabVariantBaseRefreshRow`, `PrefabVariantBaseRefreshResult`, `plan_prefab_variant_base_refresh`, `apply_prefab_variant_base_refresh`, `make_prefab_variant_base_refresh_action`, and `make_prefab_variant_base_refresh_ui_model` add retained `prefab_variant_base_refresh` review rows for explicit embedded-base refresh apply, preserving or retargeting overrides only by unique `PrefabNodeOverride::source_node_name` and blocking missing hints, missing or ambiguous refreshed source nodes, invalid inputs, and duplicate target node/kind keys. Strict `MK_scene` composition remains index-based. Nested prefab propagation beyond explicit base refresh, fuzzy matching, automatic merge/rebase/resolution UX, package scripts, validation recipes, in-process runtime-host embedding, renderer/RHI uploads, native handles, package streaming, broader editor native save/open dialogs outside Profiler, Scene, and Prefab Variant, and broad editor productization remain follow-up work.
- Editor AI Package Authoring Diagnostics v1: `EditorAiPackageAuthoringDiagnosticsModel` summarizes editor package candidate review, manifest descriptor rows, runtime package payload diagnostics, validation recipe status rows, and host-gated desktop smoke preflight without mutating manifests or executing package/validation scripts. It rejects mutation/execution claims as blocking diagnostics and does not make broad package cooking, runtime source parsing, play-in-editor productization, renderer/RHI handle exposure, Metal, or renderer quality ready.
- Editor AI Validation Recipe Preflight v1: `EditorAiValidationRecipePreflightModel` maps manifest `validationRecipes` and selected descriptor recipe ids to caller-supplied `run-validation-recipe` dry-run plans, host gates, missing recipe ids, blocked reasons, and unsupported claims. It is preflight-only: no arbitrary shell, no raw manifest command strings, no package script execution from editor core, no play-in-editor productization, no renderer/RHI handle exposure, no Metal readiness, and no renderer quality claim.
- Editor AI Playtest Readiness Report v1: `EditorAiPlaytestReadinessReportModel` aggregates `EditorAiPackageAuthoringDiagnosticsModel` and `EditorAiValidationRecipePreflightModel` into read-only package-authoring and validation-preflight rows with ready, blocked, or host-gated status. It reports `ready_for_operator_validation` only when no blocking diagnostics exist, and keeps validation execution, package script execution, free-form manifest edits, arbitrary shell, play-in-editor productization, renderer/RHI handle exposure, Metal readiness, and renderer quality out of scope.

Closeout uses closeout through existing evidence summary by rerunning `EditorAiPlaytestEvidenceSummaryModel` with new external evidence and observing `all_required_evidence_passed`, `remediation_required=false`, `handoff_required=false`, and `closeout_complete=true`; there is no separate remediation evidence-review row model and no separate remediation closeout-report row model.

- Renderer Resource Residency Upload Execution v1: a host-gated execution/report loop for explicitly selected cooked scene packages. It runs after `validate-runtime-scene-package`, keeps `IRhiDevice` and `SceneGpuBindingPalette` host-owned, uploads texture/mesh/material payloads through `MK_runtime_scene_rhi::execute_runtime_scene_gpu_upload`, and reports backend-neutral scene GPU upload counts/byte totals through desktop package smoke fields. It is not package streaming, broad residency budgets, public native/RHI handle access, material/shader graph authoring, live shader generation, Metal readiness, or general renderer quality.
- Renderer RHI Safe Point Resource Teardown v1: `MK_runtime_scene_rhi::execute_runtime_scene_gpu_binding_safe_point_teardown` lets hosts tear down `RuntimeSceneGpuBindingResult` resources at a safe point on the same `IRhiDevice` instance. `NullRhiDevice` deterministically invalidates retained handles through `null_mark_*` helpers for tests; real backends still require host-native destruction without exposing handles through gameplay APIs. It is not D3D12/Vulkan/Metal automatic resource destruction from `IRhiDevice`, a full lifetime-registry migration, or public native-handle access.

Registered Source Asset Cook Targets v1: `game.agent.json.registeredSourceAssetCookTargets` rows pair a reviewed `cook-registered-source-assets` intent with a `prefabScenePackageAuthoringTargets` id, `sourceRegistryPath`, `packageIndexPath`, `selectedAssetKeys`, and `dependencyExpansion` / `dependencyCooking` (`unsupported` + explicit selection, or `registry_closure` + in-registry closure). They are descriptor-only: no shell commands, no runtime source parsing, and no broad out-of-registry cooking.

It keeps source material/graph/export/HLSL inputs out of `runtimePackageFiles`, preserves shader artifact validation as a host gate, and does not add shader graph execution, live shader generation, shader compiler execution, package streaming, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, or general renderer quality claims.
- 3D Prefab Scene Package Authoring v1: descriptor-only `game.agent.json.prefabScenePackageAuthoringTargets` rows for generated `DesktopRuntime3DPackage` games and the committed desktop runtime sample. Rows sequence deterministic Scene/Prefab v2 authoring command rows, selected SourceAssetRegistry v1 asset keys, Scene v2 runtime package migration, runtime scene package validation, and host-gated desktop smoke without broad importer execution, broad/dependent cooking, runtime source parsing, material/shader graphs, live shader generation, skeletal animation, **arbitrary** GPU skinning beyond the reviewed D3D12 skinned mesh lane, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, or renderer quality claims.

- Renderer Debug Profiling Policy v1: `MK_renderer` exposes `mirakana::DebugProfilingPolicyDesc`, `mirakana::DebugProfilingPolicyPlan`, `mirakana::DebugProfilingRequestDesc`, `mirakana::DebugProfilingCaptureKind`, `mirakana::plan_debug_profiling_policy`, `mirakana::debug_profiling_policy_backend_evidence_ready`, `mirakana::BackendRendererParityPolicyRequest`, `mirakana::BackendRendererParityProofRow`, `mirakana::BackendRendererParityPolicyPlan`, `mirakana::plan_backend_renderer_parity_policy`, and `mirakana::backend_renderer_parity_proof_matches_selected_backend` to classify GPU timestamp/marker rows, CPU profile zone rows, per-backend promotion without cross-backend proof transfer, PIX/Vulkan/Metal trace/capture handoff gates, frame diagnostics, and fail-closed backend-local synchronization/shader-validation/memory-residency/profiling/package proof rows before automatic capture, production flame graphs, or crash telemetry export claims. `IRhiDevice::gpu_timestamp_ticks_per_second` and `mirakana::rhi::RhiStats` `gpu_debug_*` counters report backend-neutral profiling evidence; - Backend Renderer Parity Host Recipe Proof v1: `mirakana::BackendRendererParityProofRow::host_validation_recipe_id` anchors Metal host-gated or Apple-host-validated proof rows to a reviewed validation recipe from `shader-toolchain`, `mobile-packaging`, `renderer-metal-apple-host-evidence`, or `ios-simulator-smoke`. The renderer Metal recipe is Apple-host-gated and runs `check-apple-host-evidence.ps1 -RequireReady` plus the `ci-macos-appleclang` `MK_backend_scaffold_tests` / `MK_renderer_quality_matrix_tests` path. `mirakana::BackendRendererParityAppleMetalEnvironmentEvidenceDesc` plus `mirakana::make_backend_renderer_parity_apple_metal_environment_proofs` can map selected Apple-host `renderer-metal-apple-host-evidence` counters only into backend-local `synchronization`, `shader_validation`, and `package_evidence` proof rows. `mirakana::BackendRendererParityAppleMetalMemoryProfilingEvidenceDesc` plus `mirakana::make_backend_renderer_parity_apple_metal_memory_profiling_proofs` keeps `memory_residency` and `profiling_capture` as separate rows that become ready only with exact Apple-host heap/residency-set/capture evidence; partial evidence keeps the missing row host-gated. `plan_backend_renderer_parity_policy` now fails closed with `missing_host_validation_recipe` when Metal evidence omits that recipe id and `unreviewed_host_validation_recipe` when an arbitrary valid id is supplied, includes the recipe id in replay hashes, and still prevents D3D12/Vulkan proof from promoting Metal readiness or exposing native handles.
- Renderer GPU Memory Policy v1: `MK_renderer` exposes `mirakana::GpuMemoryPolicyDesc`, `mirakana::GpuMemoryPolicyPlan`, `mirakana::GpuMemoryRequestDesc`, `mirakana::GpuMemoryResidencyClass`, `mirakana::plan_gpu_memory_policy`, and `mirakana::gpu_memory_policy_backend_evidence_ready` to classify committed/placed/transient budget rows, declared memory budget evidence, residency pressure evidence, transient heap policy, upload-pressure rows, OS video-memory budget gates, per-backend memory-evidence gates without cross-backend proof transfer, and fail-closed diagnostics before backend execution or streaming/eviction claims. `mirakana::rhi::RhiDeviceMemoryDiagnostics` and `IRhiDevice::memory_diagnostics()` report DXGI `QueryVideoMemoryInfo` budgets/usage plus committed-resource byte estimates on D3D12 and best-effort committed-byte estimates on Vulkan; - Animation Root Motion Foundation v1: `mirakana::AnimationRootMotionSampleDesc`, `mirakana::validate_animation_root_motion_sample`, `mirakana::is_valid_animation_root_motion_sample`, and `mirakana::sample_animation_root_motion` provide deterministic root-joint start/end/delta sampling over existing `AnimationJointTrackDesc` data for translation and `rotation_z_radians`, using the same clamped interpolation and rest fallback as local-pose sampling. `mirakana::AnimationRootMotionAccumulationDesc`, `mirakana::validate_animation_root_motion_accumulation`, `mirakana::is_valid_animation_root_motion_accumulation`, and `mirakana::accumulate_animation_root_motion` add deterministic forward accumulation over finite non-negative intervals with an explicit positive clip duration. - Animation Float Transform Application v1: `mirakana::AnimationTransformCurveBinding`, `mirakana::AnimationTransformComponent`, and `mirakana::apply_float_animation_samples_to_transform3d` apply sampled scalar float curves to caller-owned `Transform3D` rows through explicit target-to-transform/component bindings. It validates duplicate sample/binding targets, missing bound samples, transform index ranges, finite values, and positive scale values before mutating output transforms. This is a gameplay-side binding helper; it does not add scene-node lookup, authored binding assets, generated-game scaffold wiring, full 3D orientation, or animation graph authoring.
- Animation Transform Binding Source v1: `MK_assets` exposes `GameEngine.AnimationTransformBindingSource.v1` through `mirakana::AnimationTransformBindingSourceDocument`, `mirakana::AnimationTransformBindingSourceRow`, `mirakana::AnimationTransformBindingComponent`, `mirakana::serialize_animation_transform_binding_source_document`, and `mirakana::deserialize_animation_transform_binding_source_document`. This is source authoring data only; it does not resolve scene nodes, cook runtime payloads, apply sampled curves, update generated-game scaffolds, or expand transform channels beyond translation xyz, rotation z, and scale xyz.

- glTF Node Transform Animation Import v1: `mirakana::import_gltf_node_transform_animation_tracks` imports LINEAR ordinary-node `translation`, z-axis-only quaternion `rotation`, and positive `scale` channels into sorted `GltfNodeTransformAnimationTrack` rows using `Vec3Keyframe` / `FloatKeyframe` data and an explicit `AssetImportMeshPresetV1`. It applies `unit_scale` to y-up translations, permutes z-up translation/scale-only channels into project components, and rejects z-up rotation channels with a stable diagnostic that directs callers to the quaternion clip path. It rejects duplicate channels, unsupported interpolation, `weights` channels, invalid time keys, non-z-axis y-up rotations, and non-positive scales. This is a tool-side keyframe import only; it does not add generated-game animation playback, full 3D orientation on the scalar path, or animation graph authoring.
- glTF Node Transform Animation Float Clip Bridge v1: `mirakana::import_gltf_node_transform_animation_float_clip` converts the same LINEAR ordinary-node TRS import into `GameEngine.AnimationFloatClipSource.v1` scalar tracks named `gltf/node/<node>/translation/x|y|z`, `gltf/node/<node>/rotation_z`, and `gltf/node/<node>/scale/x|y|z`, so existing `animation_float_clip` cook/package/runtime payloads and `MK_animation` byte-row sampling can consume them without a new cooked asset kind. It consumes the explicit mesh preset for translation/scale normalization and fails closed for z-up rotation. This does not apply tracks to scene nodes, add generated-game playback wiring, expand scalar rotation beyond Z-only, or add animation graph authoring.
- Cooked Animation Quaternion Clip v1: `MK_assets` exposes `GameEngine.AnimationQuaternionClipSource.v1` rows for selected 3D TRS tracks, `AssetKind::animation_quaternion_clip`, and `GameEngine.CookedAnimationQuaternionClip.v1` cook payloads; `MK_runtime` exposes `mirakana::runtime::runtime_animation_quaternion_clip_payload`; `MK_animation` exposes `AnimationJointTrack3dByteSource` / `make_animation_joint_tracks_3d_from_f32_bytes`; and `MK_tools::import_gltf_node_transform_animation_quaternion_clip` bridges LINEAR glTF node TRS 3D rows into that first-party path with explicit mesh-preset translation, quaternion basis, and scale normalization. Generated 3D package smoke now consumes this path through deterministic `AnimationPose3d` counters. This does not add animation graphs, retargeting, 3D IK local rotation limits/twist controls, renderer/RHI execution, or broad skeletal animation production readiness.
- Animation 3D Local Rotation Limits Twist Controls v1: `MK_animation` exposes `AnimationIkLocalRotationLimit3d`, `AnimationIkLocalRotationLimit3dDiagnostic`, `validate_animation_ik_local_rotation_limits_3d`, `is_valid_animation_ik_local_rotation_limits_3d`, and `apply_animation_local_rotation_limits_3d` for finite swing/twist descriptor validation and deterministic `AnimationPose3d` unit-quaternion clamps. `apply_animation_fabrik_ik_3d_solution_to_pose` also has a local-limit overload that reports when constraints prevent matching the solved 3D chain. This remains a host-independent pose/IK foundation; it does not add authored IK assets, animation graphs, retargeting, skeletal renderer deformation, runtime scene playback, or renderer/RHI execution.
- glTF Node Transform Animation Binding Source Bridge v1: `mirakana::import_gltf_node_transform_animation_binding_source` converts the same LINEAR ordinary-node TRS import into `GameEngine.AnimationTransformBindingSource.v1` rows whose targets match the float clip bridge and whose `node_name` values come from glTF node names or deterministic `gltf_node_<index>` fallbacks. It takes the same explicit mesh preset as the scalar float bridge so unsupported z-up rotation channels fail closed before mixed-coordinate binding rows are emitted. This is authoring metadata only; it does not resolve runtime scenes, sample curves, mutate node transforms, cook a payload, add generated-game playback wiring, expand scalar rotation beyond Z-only, or add animation graph authoring.
- Package Streaming Residency Budget Contract v1: `game.agent.json.packageStreamingResidencyTargets` rows for selected cooked runtime scene packages. Rows reference a manifest `runtimeSceneValidationTargets` id, a manifest `.geindex` package, positive resident budget intent, `safePointRequired=true`, and `mode="host-gated-safe-point"`; they do not execute broad background streaming, arbitrary eviction, dependency-driven streaming middleware, allocator/GPU budget enforcement, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, or renderer quality.
- Safe-Point Package Unload Replacement Execution v1: host-owned `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_package_safe_point_replacement` commits a preloaded pending `RuntimeAssetPackageStore` package and rebuilt `RuntimeResourceCatalogV2` together only at a safe point, rolls back invalid pending packages before active swap, and reports record counts, generation changes, stale-handle invalidation counts, and diagnostics. `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_package_safe_point_unload` clears the active package and commits an empty catalog only at a safe point, reports `RuntimePackageSafePointUnloadResult`, invalidates previous handles through generation change, discards pending replacement state only on successful active unload, and preserves pending state when no active package exists. It does not load files, cook packages, run async streaming, evict resources, execute renderer/RHI teardown, expose public native/RHI handles, claim Metal readiness, or make renderer quality ready.
- Resident package mount set: `mirakana::runtime::RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2` stores already-loaded `RuntimeAssetPackage` values under explicit non-zero `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2` ids, rejects invalid/duplicate/missing ids with deterministic diagnostics, advances a mount-set generation only on successful mount/unmount, and rebuilds `RuntimeResourceCatalogV2` through `mirakana::runtime::build_runtime_resource_catalog_v2_from_resident_mount_set` while preserving existing `RuntimePackageMountOverlay` (`first_mount_wins` / `last_mount_wins`) semantics. The lower-level `merge_runtime_asset_packages_overlay` still performs stable `AssetId`-ordered merge, dependency filtering, and dependency-edge deduplication for anonymous package vectors. This does not extend `RuntimeAssetPackageStore` with multiple active slots, perform filesystem or disk/VFS mount discovery, async streaming, eviction, hot reload, or renderer/RHI teardown.
- Resident catalog cache: `mirakana::runtime::RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2` refreshes from a `RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2`, overlay policy, and `RuntimeResourceResidencyBudgetV2`, reports `rebuilt`, `cache_hit`, `budget_failed`, or `catalog_build_failed`, reuses the cached `RuntimeResourceCatalogV2` when mount generation / overlay / budget are unchanged, and preserves the previous catalog and live handles when a changed budget fails. This remains an in-memory host-independent cache; it does not perform filesystem or disk/VFS mount discovery, async streaming, eviction, hot reload, renderer/RHI ownership, or GPU allocator enforcement.
- Resident package eviction plan: `mirakana::runtime::plan_runtime_resident_package_evictions_v2` returns a reviewed explicit candidate unmount order for a `RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2` until the projected `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2` view fits a target `RuntimeResourceResidencyBudgetV2`. It returns no-op success when the current view already fits, rejects invalid/duplicate/missing/protected candidate mount ids before partial planning, reports `budget_unreachable` when reviewed candidates are insufficient, and never mutates the live mount set or cache. This is not arbitrary/LRU eviction, background streaming, filesystem or disk/VFS mount discovery, upload/staging integration, renderer/RHI ownership, or allocator/GPU budget enforcement.
- Resident package reviewed eviction commit: `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_resident_package_reviewed_evictions_v2` applies only caller-reviewed `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2` eviction candidates to a projected `RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2` / `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2`, commits mount/cache state atomically after the final budget and catalog refresh succeed, reports `RuntimeResidentPackageReviewedEvictionCommitStatusV2`, `RuntimeResidentPackageReviewedEvictionCommitResultV2`, plan/cache subresults, generation/count/byte evidence, diagnostics, and committed state, and succeeds as a no-op when the current view already fits. Invalid, duplicate, missing, protected, insufficient, budget, and catalog-refresh failures preserve the previous live mount set and cached catalog. This does not load or discover packages, infer eviction policy, run broad/background streaming, productize hot reload, integrate upload/staging or renderer/RHI ownership, enforce GPU allocator budgets, infer content roots, or expose native handles.
- Candidate resident package mount commit: `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_package_candidate_resident_mount_v2` loads one reviewed `RuntimePackageIndexDiscoveryCandidateV2` through `load_runtime_package_candidate_v2`, preflights invalid/duplicate `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2` values before any filesystem read, refreshes a projected `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2` over a projected `RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2`, and commits the mount/cache together only after candidate load, budget, and catalog refresh succeed. Candidate validation, package load/read, invalid package index text, read exception, budget, and catalog refresh failures preserve the previous live mount set and cached catalog. This does not add package-streaming descriptors, broad/background streaming, hot reload, upload/staging package integration, renderer/RHI ownership, native handles, or broad disk/VFS package mount orchestration beyond this reviewed candidate commit.
- Candidate resident package replace commit: `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_package_candidate_resident_replace_v2` loads one reviewed `RuntimePackageIndexDiscoveryCandidateV2` through `load_runtime_package_candidate_v2`, preflights invalid/missing existing `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2` values before any filesystem read, then delegates to `commit_runtime_resident_package_replace_v2` so the existing mount slot/order/label and catalog-cache rollback contract stay aligned with already-loaded replacement. Candidate validation, package load/read, invalid package index text, read exception, candidate catalog, budget, and catalog refresh failures preserve the previous live mount set and cached catalog. This does not add package-streaming descriptors, broad/background streaming, hot reload, upload/staging package integration, renderer/RHI ownership, native handles, or broad disk/VFS package mount orchestration beyond reviewed candidate mount/replace commits.
- Resident package streaming mount commit: the resident-mount overload of `mirakana::runtime::execute_selected_runtime_package_streaming_safe_point` validates the selected package streaming descriptor, runtime scene validation preflight, preload/resource-kind/package-count hints, explicit non-zero `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2`, projected resident byte budget, and raw loaded-package catalog build before mutating `RuntimeResidentPackageMountSetV2`. On success it mounts the already-loaded package, refreshes `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2`, and reports deterministic `resident_mount`, `resident_catalog_refresh`, and resident generation rows. Invalid or duplicate mount ids, hint failures, package load failures, duplicate loaded-package records, catalog build failures, and projected budget failures preserve the previous mount set and cached catalog. This does not add broad filesystem/VFS package mount orchestration beyond reviewed candidate resident mount/replacement, background streaming, eviction, upload/staging package integration, renderer/RHI ownership, hot reload, or native handles.
- Resident package replacement commit: `mirakana::runtime::commit_runtime_resident_package_replace_v2` replaces one existing `RuntimeResidentPackageMountIdV2` with an already-loaded candidate package while preserving its mount slot/order, preflighting raw candidate catalog validity before overlay merge, refreshing `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2`, and reporting deterministic invalid id, missing id, candidate catalog failure, budget failure, and catalog refresh rows. Failed replacements preserve the previous mount set and cached catalog. This is the host-independent safe-point mutation needed by later hot reload/recook controllers; it does not add file watching, broad/background streaming, eviction, upload/staging package integration, renderer/RHI ownership or teardown, broad disk/VFS package mount orchestration beyond reviewed candidate resident mount/replacement, or native handles.
- Resident package streaming replace commit: `mirakana::runtime::execute_selected_runtime_package_streaming_resident_replace_safe_point` connects the selected package-streaming descriptor preflight to `commit_runtime_resident_package_replace_v2`. It validates runtime scene preflight, loaded package success, residency hints, and an existing mount id before mutation, preserves the mount slot/label and refreshes `RuntimeResidentCatalogCacheV2` on success, reports `resident_replace` status and diagnostics, and preserves the previous mount set/cache on invalid, missing, candidate catalog, budget, or cache-refresh failure. This does not add file watching, broad/background package streaming, eviction, upload/staging package integration, renderer/RHI ownership or teardown, broad disk/VFS package mount orchestration beyond reviewed candidate resident mount/replacement, or native handles.
- Runtime resource residency budget execution: `mirakana::runtime::estimate_runtime_asset_package_resident_bytes` sums cooked `RuntimeAssetRecord::content` sizes as the canonical coarse resident-byte estimate shared with host-gated package streaming checks. `mirakana::runtime::evaluate_runtime_resource_residency_budget` applies optional `RuntimeResourceResidencyBudgetV2` caps on those bytes and on merged asset row counts without eviction. `mirakana::runtime::build_runtime_resource_catalog_v2_from_resident_mounts_with_budget` merges mounts, runs the budget check, and rebuilds `RuntimeResourceCatalogV2` only when the check passes, leaving the prior catalog unchanged on failure. It does not enforce GPU allocator budgets, OS memory pressure, async eviction, or renderer/RHI teardown.
- Host-Gated Package Streaming Execution v1: `mirakana::runtime::execute_selected_runtime_package_streaming_safe_point` consumes one selected descriptor, requires successful runtime scene validation preflight, accepts an already loaded runtime package result, rejects invalid/unsafe descriptors and over-budget intent with deterministic diagnostics, and supports the original single-store package/catalog replacement path plus resident mount-set mount/replace/unmount commit paths. Renderer/RHI upload and teardown remain host-owned/planned; broad background streaming, arbitrary eviction policy, dependency-driven streaming middleware, allocator/GPU budget enforcement, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, and general renderer quality remain unsupported.
- 2D Atlas Tilemap Package Authoring v1: `game.agent.json.atlasTilemapAuthoringTargets` rows, `GameEngine.Tilemap.v1` metadata, `AssetKind::tilemap` package entries, `tilemap_texture` dependency edges, generated 2D package template rows, and runtime inspection of atlas texture kind/path/edge are ready for deterministic data-only tilemap package metadata. 2D Tilemap Editor Runtime UX v1 adds deterministic visible-cell package sampling through `mirakana::runtime::sample_runtime_tilemap_visible_cells`, editor-core package diagnostics through `mirakana::editor::make_editor_tilemap_package_diagnostics_model`, and `--require-tilemap-runtime-ux` package smoke counters such as `tilemap_cells_sampled` and `tilemap_diagnostics`. Source image decoding, production atlas packing, a full tilemap editing canvas, package streaming execution, public native/RHI handles, Metal readiness, and renderer quality remain unsupported or host-gated.
- 2D Sprite Batch Planning Contract v1 plus Sprite Batching Renderer v1: `mirakana::plan_sprite_batches` provides a host-independent, order-preserving planning pass over `mirakana::SpriteCommand` rows with adjacent compatible run coalescing, draw/texture-bind counts, atlas-backed repeated-run evidence (`atlas_backed_batch_count`, `repeated_atlas_batch_count`, `repeated_atlas_sprite_count`), and fail-closed diagnostics for invalid texture metadata, unsupported reordering policy, and required-atlas rows that contain untextured sprites. `mirakana::plan_sprite_batch_budget_profile` evaluates selected world/UI/effects `SpriteBatchBudgetProfile` rows over existing plans and fails closed for missing plans, invalid budgets, plan diagnostics, and sprite/draw/texture-bind budget excess. This remains planning/budget evidence and does not execute native GPU batches, sort transparent sprites, pack atlases, decode images, expose native/RHI handles, make Metal ready, or claim production renderer quality.
- 2D Sprite Batch Package Telemetry v1: `mirakana::plan_scene_sprite_batches` applies the existing planning contract to `mirakana::SceneRenderPacket` sprite rows through `MK_scene_renderer`, and `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` emits `sprite_batch_plan_*` smoke counters for the cooked 2D package, including `sprite_batch_plan_atlas_backed_batches`, `sprite_batch_plan_repeated_atlas_batches`, and `sprite_batch_plan_repeated_atlas_sprites` for adjacent atlas-backed rows. Sprite Batching Renderer v1 adds package-visible `sprite_batch_budget_*` counters for world, UI, and effects lane budget rows alongside selected native execution counters. This is selected telemetry/budget/execution evidence and does not sort sprites, pack atlases, decode images, expose native/RHI handles, make Metal ready, or claim broad production sprite batching readiness or renderer quality.
- Sprite Animation Flipbook v1 Phase 3: `MK_scene_renderer` exposes value-only `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookClipDesc`, `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookDesc`, `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookState`, `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookSampleResult`, `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookDirectionSetRow`, `RuntimeSpriteFlipbookPlaybackRequest`, and `advance_runtime_sprite_flipbook_playback` so generated games can select cooked sprite animation clips by gameplay state and direction, override loop/clamp playback mode, and sample frame-local event rows before binding the sampled frame to scene sprite rows. `advance_runtime_sprite_flipbook` remains the lower-level named clip advance contract. `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` now reports package-visible flipbook counters through `--require-sprite-animation`, including `sprite_flipbook_direction_sets`, `sprite_flipbook_event_rows`, `sprite_flipbook_playback_modes`, `sprite_flipbook_gameplay_state_rows`, `sprite_flipbook_events_sampled`, and `sprite_flipbook_playback_diagnostics`. This does not add game-specific animation graphs, editor animation tooling, runtime source image decoding, renderer/RHI residency, native handles, or broad production sprite animation tooling.
- Sprite Sorting Layer v1: `SpriteRendererComponent` exposes `sorting_layer` and `order_in_layer`, `mirakana::build_scene_render_packet` sorts visible sprite rows deterministically through `sort_scene_render_sprites`, and `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` reports package-visible `sprite_sort_layers_applied` and `sprite_sorted_draws` counters through `--require-sprite-sorting-layer`. This is sorting metadata and telemetry only; it does not claim transparency/overdraw policy breadth, Metal parity, public RHI handles, or production renderer quality.
- Sprite 9-Slice and Tiled v1: `SpriteRendererComponent` exposes `draw_mode`, normalized `slice_border`, and tiled `tile_size`; `mirakana::expand_scene_sprite_commands` expands nine-slice and tiled sprites into multiple `SpriteCommand` rows with UV sub-rects before batch planning/submit; and `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` reports engine-backed `sprite_9slice_tiled_source_sprites`, `sprite_9slice_expanded_quads`, and `sprite_tiled_expanded_quads` counters through `--require-sprite-9slice-tiled`. This is scene metadata plus expansion telemetry only; it does not claim UI middleware, runtime source decoding, public RHI handles, Metal parity, or production renderer quality.
- Sprite Collision Hitbox v1: `mirakana::runtime::plan_runtime_sprite_collision_hitboxes` validates first-party frame-authored hitbox/hurtbox rows, frame/entity poses, finite positive AABB bounds, layer/mask policy, duplicate ids, and hit budgets before emitting deterministic hit rows plus `RuntimeGameplayInteractionEvent` values for `plan_runtime_gameplay_interactions`. `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` reports `sprite_collision_hitbox_*` counters through `--require-sprite-collision-hitbox`. This is value-only runtime collision planning; it does not parse source sprites at runtime, paint editor hitboxes, mutate scenes, execute feedback, expose native/RHI handles, or claim broad collision middleware readiness.
- Sprite Effects Particles v1: `mirakana::runtime::plan_runtime_sprite_effect_particles` validates first-party particle templates, caller-owned active particle rows, explicit spawn events, finite transforms, sprite ids, lifetime/size/color/velocity fields, and spawn/active/render budgets before emitting deterministic render rows. `mirakana::make_runtime_sprite_effect_particle_command` and `mirakana::submit_runtime_sprite_effect_particle_rows` bridge those rows to existing sprite submissions, and `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` reports `sprite_effect_particles_*` counters through `--require-sprite-effects-particles`. Damage-number glyphs, GPU particles, editor authoring, source sprite parsing, scene mutation, native handles, and broad renderer readiness remain outside this lane.
- `update-scene-package`: first-party `GameEngine.Scene.v1` `.scene` plus matching `.geindex` scene dependency rows.
- `create-material-instance`: first-party `.material` plus matching `.geindex` material dependency rows.
- `update-ui-atlas-metadata-package`: cooked `GameEngine.UiAtlas.v1` metadata plus matching `.geindex` rows.
- `run-validation-recipe`: allowlisted validation dry-run/execute through reviewed argv builders, not arbitrary shell.

## Ready And Host-Gated Game Recipes

- Ready source-tree recipes include headless gameplay, AI navigation, runtime UI, and `2d-playable-source-tree`.
- Host-gated desktop/package proofs include `2d-desktop-runtime-package`, `3d-playable-desktop-package`, `native-gpu-runtime-ui-overlay`, `native-ui-textured-sprite-atlas`, `native-ui-text-glyph-atlas`, and `native-ui-atlas-package-metadata`.
- `sample_2d_desktop_runtime_package` closes the Engine 1.0 Windows-default 2D playable vertical slice: cooked 2D scene/sprite/HUD/audio package proof, host-gated D3D12 package window smoke with packaged DXIL shader artifacts, native 2D sprite package proof through `--require-native-2d-sprites`, scene sprite batch telemetry through `sprite_batch_plan_*` counters including atlas-backed repeated-row counters, selected world/UI/effects budget profile counters through `sprite_batch_budget_*`, renderer-owned native sprite batch execution counters such as `native_2d_sprite_batches_executed`, sprite animation counters, tilemap runtime UX counters, selected sandbox package budget proof through `--require-sandbox-package-budgets` and deterministic `sandbox_package_budget_*` counters, selected D3D12 performance baseline proof through `--require-performance-baseline` and deterministic `performance_baseline_*` p95/p99 counters, selected short-soak long-run readiness proof through `--require-long-run-performance-readiness` / deterministic `long_run_readiness_*` frame, memory, diagnostics, shutdown, and zero unsupported side-effect counters, ready opt-in host soak recipe `host-2d-long-run-readiness-soak`, and strict Vulkan package window smoke with packaged SPIR-V artifacts. This remains a narrow package/presentation/execution proof; atlas editor workflow, full tilemap editing canvas, runtime image decoding, package mutation, broad package streaming execution, broad production sprite batching readiness, broad long-running readiness, broad CPU/GPU/memory optimization, cross-vendor/backend performance parity, public native/RHI handle access, Metal readiness, source-image decode execution, and general production renderer quality remain unsupported or tracked by other gap rows.
- `tools/new-game.ps1 -Template DesktopRuntime2DPackage` generates a host-gated packaged 2D gameplay scaffold with cooked sprite texture/material/audio/orthographic scene payloads, adjacent atlas-backed sprite rows for deterministic `sprite_batch_plan_atlas_backed_batches`, `sprite_batch_plan_repeated_atlas_batches`, and `sprite_batch_plan_repeated_atlas_sprites` smoke counters, deterministic data-only tilemap metadata, first-party cooked `sprite_animation` rows, `runtimePackageFiles`, `runtimeSceneValidationTargets`, `atlasTilemapAuthoringTargets`, HUD/audio/input gameplay code, `PACKAGE_FILES_FROM_MANIFEST` registration, generated 2D sprite shader source, selected-target D3D12 shader artifact metadata, an installed native 2D sprite package smoke through `--require-native-2d-sprites`, sprite animation smoke through `--require-sprite-animation`, and tilemap runtime UX smoke through `--require-tilemap-runtime-ux`. It is the supported generated 2D package surface for Engine 1.0; source image decoding, production atlas packing/editor workflow, a full tilemap editor, package streaming execution, Metal readiness, public native/RHI handles, and broader renderer quality remain outside that claim.
- `tools/new-game.ps1 -Template DesktopRuntime3DPackage` closes the Engine 1.0 Windows-default generated 3D package surface with cooked texture/mesh/material/perspective scene payloads, authored Scene/Prefab v2 source files, a selected source asset registry, `runtimePackageFiles`, `runtimeSceneValidationTargets`, `prefabScenePackageAuthoringTargets`, `packageStreamingResidencyTargets`, primary camera/controller package smoke, source material/HLSL authoring inputs kept out of runtime package files, selected-target D3D12 shader artifact metadata, Vulkan toolchain-gated package recipes, generated package-visible `scene_mesh_plan_*` telemetry, cooked scalar transform animation smoke, cooked CPU morph package smoke, cooked quaternion scene-transform package smoke through `runtime_animation_quaternion_clip_payload` / `sample_and_apply_runtime_scene_render_animation_pose_3d`, selected safe-point package streaming counters through `--require-package-streaming-safe-point`, selected scene GPU + depth-aware postprocess + renderer-quality counters, selected directional shadow package smoke through `--require-directional-shadow --require-directional-shadow-filtering` with `framegraph_render_passes_recorded=6`, selected graphics morph + directional shadow receiver smoke through `--require-shadow-morph-composition` with `renderer_gpu_morph_draws`, `renderer_morph_descriptor_binds`, `directional_shadow_ready=1`, `framegraph_passes_executed=6`, `framegraph_render_passes_recorded=6`, and `framegraph_barrier_steps_executed=15`, selected D3D12 native UI overlay HUD box smoke through `--require-native-ui-overlay`, `hud_boxes=2`, `ui_overlay_ready=1`, `ui_overlay_sprites_submitted=2`, and `ui_overlay_draws=2`, selected D3D12 cooked UI atlas image sprite smoke through `--require-native-ui-textured-sprite-atlas`, `hud_images=2`, `ui_atlas_metadata_status=ready`, `ui_texture_overlay_atlas_ready=1`, `ui_texture_overlay_sprites_submitted=2`, `ui_texture_overlay_texture_binds=2`, and `ui_texture_overlay_draws=2`, selected D3D12 cooked UI atlas text glyph smoke through `--require-native-ui-text-glyph-atlas`, `hud_text_glyphs=2`, `text_glyphs_resolved=2`, `text_glyphs_missing=0`, `ui_atlas_metadata_glyphs=1`, `ui_texture_overlay_sprites_submitted=2`, `ui_texture_overlay_texture_binds=2`, and `ui_texture_overlay_draws=2`, D3D12-primary scene GPU graphics morph smoke that ships and reads POSITION/NORMAL/TANGENT delta streams through explicit mesh-to-morph bindings, D3D12-primary compute morph package smoke that dispatches selected cooked morph rows into renderer-consumed POSITION output buffers plus explicit `scene_gpu_compute_morph_tangent_frame_output` counters, generated D3D12 skin+compute package smoke through `--require-compute-morph-skin`, skinned compute shader artifacts, a `skinned_mesh` package row, and `scene_gpu_compute_morph_skinned_*` counters, and toolchain-gated Vulkan POSITION/NORMAL/TANGENT plus skin+compute compute morph package smokes through explicit SPIR-V artifacts. It remains a scoped generated package proof and does not claim runtime source parsing, broad dependency cooking, broad async/background package streaming, material/shader graphs, live shader generation, production text shaping, font rasterization, glyph atlas generation, runtime source image decoding, source image atlas packing, broad skeletal animation, Vulkan async compute overlap/performance, Metal compute morph parity, broad production frame graph scheduling beyond selected smoke counters, graphics morph+skin composition beyond the host-owned skin+compute package smoke, broad shadow+morph composition beyond the selected receiver smoke, morph-deformed shadow-caster silhouettes, scene-schema morph authoring, generated-package 3D local rotation-limit authoring/playback wiring, Metal, native/RHI handles, broad generated 3D production readiness, or general renderer quality.
- `sample_generated_desktop_runtime_3d_package` and generated `DesktopRuntime3DPackage` scaffolds now also ship a cooked `GameEngine.PhysicsCollisionScene3D.v1` `physics_collision_scene` package row with primitive body rows, `body.N.compound` group labels, material/layer/mask/trigger metadata, and `backend.native=unsupported`. The selected `--require-scene-collision-package` smoke decodes it through `mirakana::runtime::runtime_physics_collision_scene_3d_payload`, builds a first-party `mirakana::PhysicsWorld3D` via `mirakana::runtime::build_physics_world_3d_from_runtime_collision_scene`, and requires `collision_package_status=ready`, `collision_package_bodies=3`, `collision_package_triggers=1`, `collision_package_contacts>=1`, `collision_package_trigger_overlaps>=1`, `collision_package_world_ready=1`, `collision_query_batch_ready=1`, `collision_query_readiness_status=ready`, `collision_query_readiness_diagnostic=none`, `collision_query_readiness_diagnostics=0`, source-ordered collision query batch rows, deterministic hit/no-hit/invalid-request counters, query-budget rejection counters, and `gameplay_systems_collision_package_ready=1`. `PhysicsWorld3D::contact_manifolds` now covers deterministic contact manifold rows for the first-party bodies loaded by this path, and `evaluate_physics_collision_query_readiness_3d` summarizes the selected query batch proof. CCD, dynamic controller policies, explicit distance-joint and distance/fixed/linear-axis positional constraint solving, value-only kinematic motion planning, replay signatures, and count-based determinism budget gates now live in first-party physics APIs; timing benchmarks, persistent joint assets, broad vehicle dynamics/persistent vehicle simulation APIs, ragdolls, editor physics debugging UX, oriented boxes, mesh/convex casts, middleware-native query exposure, and broad physics beyond the first-party Physics 1.0 ready surface remain follow-up work; Jolt/native middleware remains excluded from the default/generated-game Physics 1.0 ready surface; `MK_physics_jolt` now provides an optional `physics-jolt` dependency-gated adapter lane outside that ready claim for collision-enabled, non-trigger authored 3D solid scenes, with fail-closed diagnostics for single-backend-body scenes, disabled-collision bodies, triggers, unsupported Jolt filter bits, and Jolt capacity errors.
- Physics/Navigation Production Breadth Gate v1 adds `mirakana::review_physics_production_breadth` in `MK_physics` and `mirakana::review_navigation_production_breadth` in `MK_navigation` as value-only audit gates for post-1.0 production-breadth promotion. They require reviewed official-source URLs, package counter ids, host validation or explicit host-gated rows, deterministic replay/path evidence, positive budgets, dependency/legal records, `adapter_boundary_id`, `host_validation_recipe_id`, and `adapter_lifecycle_reviewed` for optional native/Jolt/Recast/Detour-class adapter rows. They fail closed on missing evidence, native handle exposure, source-geometry mutation, arbitrary runtime-bake claims, and broad middleware parity claims. This is not runtime importer/bake/execution, package mutation, generated-game broad readiness, or a claim that physics/navigation is now commercial-game complete across all genres.
- D3D12 is the strongest Windows-validated visible/package lane.
- Vulkan package and visible claims require strict host/runtime/toolchain validation.
- Android Release Device Matrix v1 gives Android GameActivity packaging current Windows host evidence for `sample_headless`: `pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File tools/validate-android-gameactivity-host.ps1 -Game sample_headless -RunPackageCommands -RequireReady -StartEmulator -AvdName GameEngine_API36 -AndroidAbi x86_64 -ValidationLayerJniLibs out/host-artifacts/android-validation-layers/jniLibs` passes and emits `android_gameactivity_mobile_check_ready=1`, `android_gameactivity_validation_layer_jni_libs_ready=1`, `android_gameactivity_debug_build_ready=1`, `android_gameactivity_release_package_ready=1`, `android_gameactivity_release_smoke_ready=1`, and `android_gameactivity_host_ready=1`; default invocation is non-mutating and stays fail-closed. `tools/prepare-android-vulkan-validation-layers.ps1` shapes host-supplied official Khronos Android validation-layer release binaries into ignored `out/host-artifacts/android-validation-layers/jniLibs/<abi>/libVkLayer_khronos_validation.so` for stricter Android package/readback validators.
